     1	# Phase 3 — Complete Restructuring Proposal: nirs4all Documentation & Examples
     2	
     3	**Date:** 2026-06-04 · **Inputs:** `02_audit.md` (Codex-signed-off), `GROUND_TRUTH.md`
     4	**Method:** 3 competing IA candidates (distinct philosophies) → 4-lens judge panel → grounded synthesis → page-by-page migration map (9 agents). Codex-gated.
     5	**Raw data:** `data/proposal_*.json`. **Status:** complete; Codex review round 3 pending.
     6	
     7	---
     8	
     9	## 0. Executive summary
    10	
    11	The audit proved the corpus is *conceptually strong but structurally sprawling and mechanically rotten*: 4 competing front doors, `api/`↔`reference/` documenting the same surface twice, ~648 inline-style violations, ~15 copy-paste-fatal wrong-API snippets, and — the root cause — **nothing executes documentation**, so all of it ships silently.
    12	
    13	This proposal adopts a **hybrid architecture** that the judge panel converged on, because the three philosophies each won a different decisive lens and the hybrid takes each winner where it is strongest:
    14	
    15	> **A strict-Diátaxis single-source-of-truth backbone, carrying a FastAPI-style progressive Tutorial spine as its Tutorials arm, with the Reference and Examples estates generated from source/disk, and verb/goal routing demoted to navigation-only.**
    16	
    17	- **Diátaxis** (Tutorials / How-to / Reference / Explanation as four non-overlapping *modes*) is the backbone because it is the only candidate that makes single-source-of-truth a **structural invariant** — *"Explanation owns the why, Reference owns the signature; neither restates the other, the only permitted relationship is a hyperlink"* — and gives a **mechanical placement rule** for any new page. This dissolves the audit's #6 (competing front doors) and #18 (api↔reference duplication) *by construction*, not by editorial vigilance.
    18	- **FastAPI's single linear Tutorial rail** is grafted as the Tutorials arm because strict Diátaxis scored *lowest* on newcomer onboarding (four equal mode cards reproduce today's confusing grid). The rail gives one CTA per on-ramp page, one new concept per lesson, every step a runnable inline `run()`, and a structurally pre-decided "Next →".
    19	- **Generate-from-source** (autosummary-recursive over the 357 API symbols; sphinx-gallery over `examples/*.py`) is adopted for the drift-prone Reference and Examples estates — *generated-not-handwritten is the only true zero-drift mechanism*, and it self-heals the audit's stale counts (#16), undocumented examples (#17), and missing R04 (#34).
    20	- **Verb/goal/persona routing** (the task-first candidate's idea) is kept as **navigation cards + "Next goals →" links**, never as duplicated content tracks — which is exactly what kept that candidate lowest on maintainability.
    21	
    22	The work is sequenced so **correctness lands before structure**: P0 metadata + wrong-API triage (1–2 days, no IA change), P1 style sweep + lint, P2 safety-net CI, then P3 the structural IA migration, P4 reference unification. Definition of done is measurable (§9): 0 style violations, 0 stale versions, exactly one front door, one Reference home, all snippets execute in CI, mean health ≥ 4/5.
    23	
    24	---
    25	
    26	## 1. How the architecture was chosen (panel result)
    27	
    28	Three complete IAs were designed independently, then scored 1–10 by four judges, each through one lens:
    29	
    30	| Candidate | Newcomer onboarding | Maintainability/SSOT | Fit to API surface | Enforceability | Outcome |
    31	|---|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|---|
    32	| **1 — Strict Diátaxis** | 6 | **9** | 8 | **9** | Won SSOT + enforceability; *lost* onboarding (4 equal cards fragment topics). |
    33	| **2 — Tutorial-first (FastAPI)** | **9** | 7 | **9** | **9** | Won onboarding + fit + enforceability; risk of teach-vs-explain duplication. |
    34	| **3 — Task/persona-first** | 8 | 6 | 8 | 8 | Best anti-drift *generation* idea; but 7 task tracks re-invite concept duplication. |
    35	
    36	The lenses split cleanly, so the synthesis is a **hybrid, not a single winner**: Candidate 1's SSOT skeleton + placement law as the spine; Candidate 2's linear rail + executable gallery + IA-agnostic CI gates as the Tutorials arm and safety net; Candidate 3's generate-from-source as the *implementation* of Reference and Examples; its task routing demoted to navigation. This is the standard best-practice resolution (it is, in effect, how Django, FastAPI, scikit-learn, and Polars docs actually compose these patterns).
    37	
    38	**Patterns borrowed, named:** Diátaxis four-mode split + SSOT law (backbone); FastAPI tutorial-first single rail, one-CTA-per-page, one-concept-per-page, every-snippet-runnable (Tutorials arm); scikit-learn User-Guide(How-to) + API-Reference + executable-gallery separation; Polars/Pydantic mkdocs-material clarity + per-page mode badges; scikit-learn/sphinx generate-from-source for zero drift.
    39

    42	## 2. Target information architecture
    43	
    44	```
    45	Start here  (index.md — THIN ROUTER; teaches nothing)
    46	├─ "Start here → first run"  (the single primary CTA)
    47	└─ "I already have a goal →"  (nav links into Tutorial/How-to/Reference — no content)
    48	
    49	Get Started / first run   (install + ZERO-DATA generate.regression() inline run(); only forward link: "Continue to the Tutorial →")
    50	
    51	Tutorial   (learning-oriented · single linear FastAPI rail · prev/next · one new concept/lesson · every step a runnable inline run() · mode badge · sideways "Why it works →" Explanation + "Run this yourself →" Gallery)
    52	   L1 Your first model (swap synthetic → your own folder)   L8  Visualization
    53	   L2 Preprocessing (SNV)                                    L9  Hyperparameter tuning (generators)
    54	   L3 Datasets & loading                                     L10 Branching & merging
    55	   L4 Cross-validation                                       L11 Augmentation
    56	   L5 Models & scoring/refit                                 L12 Export & deploy (.n4a, predict reuse)
    57	   L6 Reading results & predict()                            L13 Retrain & transfer (full|transfer|finetune)
    58	   L7 Classification
    59	
    60	How-to guides   (task-oriented recipes · goal-titled · self-contained · NO concept-teaching, link to Explanation · NO "why")
    61	   Data · Preprocessing · Models · Pipelines · Augmentation · Predictions · Deployment · Visualization · Operations · Troubleshooting
    62	
    63	Reference   (information-oriented · GENERATED where possible · ONE home — api/ dissolved into it)
    64	   Syntax & keywords · Operator catalog · Public-API contract pages · reference/api/ (357 autosummary-recursive stubs) · Configuration · Storage & workspace · Session · Metrics · CLI
    65	
    66	Explanation   (understanding-oriented · the SINGLE canonical concept home · read not run · links DOWN to Reference, never restates a signature)
    67	   pipelines · datasets · cross_validation · branching_and_merging · generators · augmentation · predictions_and_deployment · mental_models/overview · workspace & reproducibility
    68	
    69	Examples gallery   (executable · sphinx-gallery over examples/*.py · tagged by lesson/recipe · counts derived from disk)
    70	   User (U) track → lessons/recipes   ·   Reference (R) track → Reference pages   ·   (Developer D track lives under Contributing)
    71	
    72	Contributing & internals   (separate audience · NEVER a user front door · internally split by the same four modes)
    73	   Architecture · Extending (controllers, custom operators) · Internals (caching, artifacts, metadata, synthetic) · Testing & dev gallery · Documentation style (STYLE.md) · Migration
    74	
    75	About   (all metadata source-derived)   changelog · license (dual, default AGPL-3.0-or-later) · citation · roadmap pointer
    76	
    77	llms.txt   (non-nav machine on-ramp; ex ai_onboarding.md; regenerated from canonical anchors)
    78	```

    82	## 3. The single front door (resolving audit #6)
    83	
    84	Today: **four** competing front doors (`getting_started/`, `concepts/`, `onboarding/`, `ai_onboarding.md`) plus a 6-card landing grid; foundational concepts taught 3–4×. Resolution:
    85	
    86	1. **`index.md` becomes a thin router** — one prominent *"Start here → first run"* CTA, four secondary Diátaxis mode cards + one Examples card, and a small *"I already have a goal →"* nav block (the only surviving trace of persona routing — navigation, not content). It teaches nothing.
    87	2. **One Get-Started page** whose only forward link is *"Continue to the Tutorial →"*: `pip install nirs4all`, then the literal first copy-paste, which **succeeds with zero user data** because the dataset is synthetic:
    88	   ```python
    89	   result = nirs4all.run(
    90	       pipeline=[MinMaxScaler(), ShuffleSplit(n_splits=3), {"model": PLSRegression(n_components=10)}],
    91	       dataset=nirs4all.generate.regression(n_samples=500),
    92	   )
    93	   print(result.best_rmse)
    94	   ```
    95	   This snippet is **`literalinclude`-tied to a CI-run example**, so it can never rot the way `result.predict()` (#3) did.
    96	3. **Tutorial L1 changes exactly one thing** — swap the synthetic dataset for the user's own folder path — and the prev/next rail makes every "second task" structurally pre-decided.
    97	4. **Concrete deletions that make the single door real:** `getting_started/concepts.md` DELETED (residue → Explanation); `persona_paths.md` DELETED (its fake `load_dataset()` #7 and 5 broken refs #8 die with it); `onboarding/` DISSOLVED into Explanation + Contributing; `ai_onboarding.md` removed from the human toctree → `llms.txt`.
    98	
    99	Net: **exactly one Start-here, exactly one conceptual home (Explanation), zero front-door overlap.**

   102	
   103	## 4. The governing law (so it stays fixed)
   104	
   105	Two rules, adopted verbatim from the maintainability-winning candidate, are what convert this from a one-off cleanup into durable governance:
   106	
   107	- **SSOT law:** *Explanation owns the "why"; Reference owns the signature/parameters; neither restates the other — the only permitted relationship is a hyperlink.* (This single sentence is the most drift-proof artifact in the exercise; it makes #6 and #18 structurally impossible to recreate.)
   108	- **Placement rule (Contributing checklist):** a new page is filed by the *reader's posture* — learning → Tutorial, doing-a-task → How-to, looking-up → Reference, understanding → Explanation. Topic-agnostic, so a future contributor knows where a new page goes without judgment.
   109	
   110	---
   111	
   112	## 5. The style guide (the 648-violation defect → infrastructure)
   113	
   114	**THE RULE** (stated once in `STYLE.md`, shown on the first Get-Started snippet, then enforced mechanically, never re-explained per page): every code block that runs a pipeline writes it **inline in one shot inside `run()`**, no external variable.
   115	
   116	```python
   117	result = nirs4all.run(pipeline=[ ...inline steps... ], dataset=...)   # ✅
   118	pipeline = [ ... ]; nirs4all.run(pipeline, ds)                        # ❌ forbidden
   119	```
   120	
   121	**THE DOCUMENTED EXCEPTIONS** (machine-readable in `STYLE.md`, which *is* the allowlist the lint reads; plus per-site `# noqa: inline-pipeline` markers with a reason, so the carve-out is auditable and cannot silently widen):
   122	1. deliberate **reuse/comparison** running the same pipeline through several `run()`/`PipelineRunner`/`Session` calls, or a **list-of-pipelines** (a handful in `06_deployment`/`06_internals`; **plus the verified false positive `writing_pipelines.md:1242` `run(pipeline=[pipeline_pls, pipeline_rf, pipeline_nn])`**);
   123	2. **synthesis/utility** scripts that are not pipeline tutorials (`developer/02_generators/D05–D09`, `examples/_internal/*`);
   124	3. compliant inline calls merely **split across multiple physical lines** (which a naive grep false-positives on — Codex's 605-vs-655 note).
   125	
   126	**THE CI LINT — the exact pattern to flag:** a statement-level assignment whose target name contains `pipeline` and whose value is a **list literal**, where that same name is later passed **positionally** as the first arg to `run()`/`PipelineRunner()`. It must **not** flag (i) `pipeline=[` keyword args (the compliant inline form), (ii) `run(pipeline=[a, b, c])` list-of-pipelines, (iii) multi-line inline calls. **Precision is load-bearing:** the naive `pipeline = [` grep yields ~648–655 candidate sites but only **3 truly-compliant `run(pipeline=[`** exist in docs — a sloppy gate floods false positives and gets disabled.
   127	
   128	**Order:** one mechanical sweep clears the ~648 *before* the gate turns on (CI starts green); thereafter the gate prevents regrowth — without it, 648 → 700 next release.
   129	
   130	---
   131	
   132	## 6. Examples plan (the executable backbone)
   133	
   134	- **Gallery, not prose.** The ~80 `examples/*.py` are the single source of truth (they already double as integration tests) and are rendered into a **sphinx-gallery** generated *from* the scripts. The **8 hand-written `docs/source/examples/*.md` wrappers are DELETED and regenerated** — they had drifted (stale counts #16, undocumented U05/U06 #17, `SklearnWrapper` #12, U21/U22 #15). Because the rendered snippet *is* the CI-run file, the documented-vs-tested gap is structurally closed.
   135	- **Embed, don't duplicate.** Each Tutorial lesson links *"Run this yourself →"* to its backing U-file; each How-to recipe links to its script; each Reference page links to its canonical R-example.
   136	- **R04 fix (#34/#14):** convert the stale 1.8 MB health-1/5 `examples/predictions.ipynb` into a runnable `examples/reference/R04_visualization.py` on the public `PredictionAnalyzer` API — fills the missing-R04 gap and deletes the broken un-CI'd notebook in one move.
   137	- **Weekly → per-PR CI (#19):** replace `examples.yml`'s Sunday cron (`0 0 * * 0`) with a **fast tagged U+R subset on every push/PR** (~7–10 files); the full ~80-file suite stays nightly/weekly. No gallery script sits broken on `main` for 7 days.
   138	- **Must-call-`run()` gate (#32):** every `examples/**.py` either calls `run()`/`PipelineRunner`/`Session` **or** carries an explicit `# syntax-only` marker (verified: `D01_metadata_branching`, `D03_repetition_transform` have 0 `run()` calls — a "runs without error" check would pass them silently).
   139	- **One disk-derived manifest** feeds `run.sh`, `run_ci_examples.sh`, README, and the gallery — the count is stamped once everywhere (#16).
   140

   144	
   145	`api/` is **deleted, not maintained beside `reference/`** — explicit acceptance criterion: *"two trees documenting one surface is structurally impossible afterward."*
   146	
   147	- **Autodoc:** replace the 357 hand-touched `api/*.rst` stubs with **one autosummary-recursive root mounted under `reference/api/`** — adding a public symbol updates the reference with zero manual edits.
   148	- **Hand-written `api/*.md` merged then deleted:** `api/storage.md` (~794 LOC, "Version 5.0", legacy `runs/`) → `reference/storage.md`; `api/workspace.md` (100%-duplicate PipelineLibrary) → `reference/workspace.md`; `api/module_api.md` → curated public-API pages (fixing predict() first param `source`→`model` #22); `api/sklearn_integration.md` → `reference/` sklearn page.
   149	- **`reference/api/session.md`** wired into `reference/index` (fixes orphan #26).

   151	- **Curated contract pages** for the stable public surface own narrative + signatures; `run()` completed with the 4 missing params `refit/cache/project/report_naming` (#23); `cli.md` drops the `- runs/` line (#24).
   152	- **Docstring fixes at source** so autodoc stops inheriting stale calls: `Predictions.load()` in `visualization/predictions.py:76` → `from_parquet`/`from_file`/`from_workspace` (#14).

   154	---
   155	
   156	## 8. Safety-net CI (the root-cause fix — five per-PR gates)
   157	
   158	The audit's §5.3 root cause: *nothing that executes documentation exists.* Five gates convert the entire "ships silently" class into build failures:
   159	
   160	1. **Doc-snippet execution via `literalinclude`-from-tested-examples (primary).** The rendered snippet is a slice of a CI-run `examples/*.py`, so doc/example drift is impossible by construction (defeats #3/#4/#9/#12/#14). `myst_nb`/doctest with tiny `generate.regression()` fixtures + `plots_visible=False` is reserved only for snippets that genuinely cannot be a whole runnable file.
   161	2. **Per-PR examples (#19) + must-call-`run()` gate (#32).**
   162	3. **Nitpick tightening (#19/§5.3A):** remove the blanket `nitpick_ignore_regex` masking `nirs4all.{data,pipeline,api}.*` and the `myst.xref_missing`/`ref.*` suppressions so a typo'd `:class:` ref **fails** the build; reconcile the verified contradiction — `docs.yml` builds `-W --keep-going` (strict) while `.readthedocs.yaml` sets `fail_on_warning: false` — to the same strictness (RTD → `true`). Expect a backlog of real broken refs to burn down first (staged after P4).
   163	4. **Metadata-from-source + grep gates:** `conf.py` `release` read from `nirs4all.__version__`; license/citation templated from `LICENSE` in one place; a CI grep asserts the rendered license **string matches** the `LICENSE` dual-license statement **without banning the legitimate `CeCILL` token** (audit #1, GROUND_TRUTH); fails if any version string ≠ `__version__`.
   164	5. **Precise inline-style lint (§5) + broken-example-ref gate + example-count stamp.** The ref-gate greps that every `examples/*.py` path referenced in docs exists on disk (catches #8, #15 — a wrong *path* in prose isn't executable, so doc-execution can't catch it).
   165

     1	# Ground-Truth Card — nirs4all public surface (verified from source)
     2	
     3	**Verified:** 2026-06-04 by reading source (no memory, no guessing). `nirs4all/__init__.py`, `nirs4all/api/*.py`. Corrected after Codex review round 2.
     4	**Version:** `0.9.1` (`nirs4all/__init__.py:45`). Any doc pinning `0.2.1` / `0.7.1` / `0.8.6` / `0.9.0` / "5.0" is STALE.
     5	**License:** the project is **DUAL-licensed** (`LICENSE:1-13`): open-source **default `AGPL-3.0-or-later`** (optional `GPL-3.0-or-later` / `CeCILL-2.1` variants) **plus** a separate commercial license. So `CeCILL-2.1` is NOT "wrong" — it is a legitimate *optional* variant. The defect is pages that present `CeCILL-2.1` as the *sole/default* license (the default is AGPL-3.0-or-later). Do NOT add a CI gate banning the `CeCILL` token; gate instead on the landing/citation license string matching the `LICENSE` dual-license statement.
     6	
     7	Audit agents: treat this card as authoritative. If a doc/example names a symbol, path, or signature that contradicts this card, that is a **defect**. If something is not on this card, verify against source before flagging.

     1	# Phase 2 — Exhaustive Audit of nirs4all Documentation & Examples
     2	
     3	**Date:** 2026-06-04 · **Library version of record:** 0.9.1 · **License of record:** AGPL-3.0
     4	**Method:** ground-truth-first, 22-agent grounded fan-out, adversarial completeness critic, manual verification pass, Codex-gated.
     5	**Status:** complete. Raw data in `data/` (`audit_segments.json`, `audit_synthesis.json`, `audit_completeness_critic.json`). Ground-truth card in `GROUND_TRUTH.md`.
     6	
     7	---
     8	
     9	## 0. Verdict
    10	
    11	The corpus is **broad, conceptually strong, and NOT publication-ready.** Mean segment health is **2.80 / 5** across 20 audited segments. The content (concepts, reference tables, scientific prose) is largely *accurate and complete*; what drags it down is **mechanical rot and structural sprawl**, not wrong ideas. Three systemic failures compound to mislead a newcomer within the first ten minutes:
    12	
    13	1. **Metadata drift on first-contact surfaces** — the license is **mis-stated** (the project is *dual-licensed*: default `AGPL-3.0-or-later`, with `GPL-3.0`/`CeCILL-2.1` optional variants + a commercial license per `LICENSE:1-13`; but the landing page, AI-onboarding page, and root `CLAUDE.md` present `CeCILL-2.1` as the **sole** license) and the version is wrong (0.2.1 / 0.7.1 / 0.8.6 / 0.9.0 / "5.0" instead of 0.9.1) on the landing page, the citation block, the AI-onboarding page, and `conf.py`. A mis-stated license on the landing page is a compliance issue, not a typo.
    14	2. **The inline-pipeline style mandate is violated 648 times across 140 files** (authoritative grep, §3). *No segment is fully clean.* The docs teach, at scale, the exact anti-pattern the project wants forbidden.
    15	3. **Copy-paste-fatal wrong-API references** scattered through the on-ramp and how-to layers (`result.predict()`, `nirs4all.load_dataset()`, `bundle=`, `y_column=`, `PredictionAnalyzer.plot_predictions()`, `GaussianNoise`, `SklearnWrapper`, `examples.synthetic` import, `Predictions.load()` in the shipped notebook) — every one verified against source as non-existent.
    16	
    17	Underlying all three is one root cause: **nothing that executes documentation exists in the safety net.** Doc `.md` code blocks are never run; the `examples/*.py` suite (which *does* run) is on a **weekly** schedule, not per-PR; and the Sphinx build actively **suppresses** broken cross-references (`nitpick_ignore_regex` blankets entire `nirs4all.*` namespaces). So every defect above survived precisely because nothing could catch it.
    18	
    19	The good news, and the reason a rewrite is tractable: the failures are **overwhelmingly mechanical and high-reach/low-effort**. A metadata one-commit fix, one mechanical inline-pipeline sweep, a ~15-item wrong-API triage, and a CI gate to stop regression clear the majority. The structural work (collapsing the competing front doors) is design, not archaeology. This audit is the input to the Phase 3 restructuring proposal.
    20	
    21	---
    22	
    23	## 1. Methodology
    24	
    25	Why this much machinery: the user asked for an audit that is *detailed, structured, exhaustive, and justified*, reviewed by Codex at each step. Documentation audits fail in two classic ways — (a) the auditor hallucinates the API and "corrects" things that are actually fine, and (b) coverage is uneven so whole areas are silently skipped. We defended against both:
    26	
    27	- **Ground-truth-first.** Before any agent ran, the real public surface was extracted *directly from source* (`nirs4all/__init__.py`, `nirs4all/api/*.py`, `api/result.py`) into `GROUND_TRUTH.md` — exact `__all__`, signatures, result-object members, the canonical style form. Every agent was required to Read it and to cite the source/ground-truth fact proving each defect (the `evidence` field). No claim rests on memory.
    28	- **Deterministic fan-out.** The doc+example surface was partitioned into **20 segments with explicit, non-overlapping file lists** (12 documentation · 6 examples · 2 root/build) so coverage is provable, not best-effort. One `Explore` (read-only) reader per segment, run in parallel, each grounding against source.
    29	- **Cross-cutting synthesis** (1 agent, barrier): merged duplicate findings, quantified repo-wide patterns, built the prioritized register.
    30	- **Adversarial completeness critic** (1 agent): tasked only with finding what the audit *missed or over-claimed*.
    31	- **Manual verification pass** (this orchestrator, against source): resolved every dispute the critic raised, ran the authoritative style-violation grep, and audited the surfaces the fan-out had missed (the notebook, the hand-written `api/*.md` pages, build hygiene).
    32	- **Codex gate:** the finished audit is handed to Codex (`codex exec`, CLI 0.136.0) for independent adversarial review before Phase 3. Transcript archived under `codex_reviews/`.
    33	
    34	**Run cost (audit workflow):** 22 agents, ~1.73M agent tokens, 1011 tool calls, ~11 min wall-clock. 20/20 segment readers returned. Plus 3 gap-closing agents and the manual verification pass.
    35	
    36	### 1.1 The completeness critic earned its keep — corrections applied
    37	
    38	The critic caught **two false "critical release blockers"** and a **false "clean segment"** claim in the raw synthesis. All three were independently re-verified against source and **corrected** in this document (full transparency in §6):
    39	
    40	| Raw claim | Verdict after verification | Source proof |
    41	|---|---|---|
    42	| "Uninstantiated transform classes → runtime crash" (U01_shap_basics.py) | **FALSE — downgraded.** Bare class types are an *intentional, supported* pipeline form. | `nirs4all/pipeline/steps/parser.py:231` "Class types: returns as-is (controller will instantiate)"; the file is in both CI runners and passes. |
    43	| "Two broken transfer-learning imports → ImportError crash, release blocker" | **PARTLY FALSE — downgraded to medium.** Both imports are inside `try/except ImportError`; they don't crash. But the module paths *are* wrong, so the feature is silently never demonstrated. | `examples/developer/04_transfer_learning/D01_transfer_analysis.py:130-152` (try/except). Real homes: `nirs4all.analysis.selector.TransferPreprocessingSelector`, `nirs4all.visualization.analysis.transfer.PreprocPCAEvaluator`. |
    44	| "Only 2 segments are style-clean; ~250+ violations" | **FALSE.** predictions/deployment is *not* clean; the real count is **648** (§3). | grep of `making_predictions.md:246`, `session_api.md:30,217`; authoritative count in §3. |
    45	
    46	This is the audit doing its job: the multi-agent pass surfaced ~216 candidate defects fast, and the adversarial+manual layer pruned the wrong ones before they could waste a maintainer's time. **Act on the corrected register (§4), not the raw per-segment files.**
    47	
    48	---

    50	## 2. Scope & coverage
    51	
    52	### What was audited (provably complete surface)
    53	
    54	| Layer | Count | Coverage |
    55	|---|---|---|
    56	| Documentation narrative `.md` (`docs/source/**`, excl. `api/`) | ~119 pages | 12 segments, explicit file lists |
    57	| Hand-written `api/*.md` + `reference/api/session.md` | 5 pages | gap-closing pass (§5.2) |
    58	| Auto-generated `api/*.rst` autodoc stubs | 357 | assessed structurally (build segment + §5.3) |
    59	| Executable examples `examples/**/*.py` | ~80 user/dev/reference + infra | 6 segments |
    60	| Shipped notebook `examples/predictions.ipynb` | 1 (1.8 MB) | gap-closing pass (§5.1) |
    61	| Root/meta (`README`, `INSTALLATION`, `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `CONTRIBUTING`, `Roadmap`, `CHANGELOG`) | 7 | 1 segment |
    62	| Build/RTD config (`conf.py`, `Makefile`, `build_docs.sh`, `.readthedocs.yaml`, CI workflows) | — | build segment + §5.3 |
    63	| Assets (`docs/source/assets/`) | 28 | reference-integrity check (§5.3) |
    64	
    65	### Genuinely out of scope (stated, not skipped)
    66	
    67	- **i18n:** there is no FR/EN duplication (no `locale/`, no `*.fr.md`, single-language `conf.py`) — nothing to audit. The root *repo* ships FR variants (`CLA_FR.md`, `CONTRIBUTING_FR.md`, `THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES_FR.md`) but the *docs site* is English-only.
    68	- **Versioned-docs divergence** (stable vs latest RTD builds) beyond the single stale `release` string — not examined; flagged as a follow-up.

    70	---
    71	
    72	## 3. The inline-pipeline style mandate — authoritative measurement
    73	
    74	> **Mandate (user, verbatim intent):** "1 pipeline, des datasets, run()." Pipelines must be written **inline, in one shot**, inside `run()`, with **no external variable**, for readability:
    75	> ```python
    76	> result = nirs4all.run(pipeline=[ ...inline... ], dataset=...)   # ✅
    77	> ```
    78	> ```python
    79	> pipeline = [ ... ]                 # ❌ external variable
    80	> result = nirs4all.run(pipeline, dataset)
    81	> ```
    82	
    83	The raw synthesis estimated "250+ violations, only 2 clean segments." That was wrong (the critic flagged it; one reader's grep was non-uniform). A single uniform grep across `docs/source/**.md` and `examples/**.py` (variable name contains `pipeline`, assigned a list literal at statement level) gives the authoritative figure:
    84	
    85	### **~648 candidate sites across 140 files. No segment is clean. Only 55 compliant inline `run(pipeline=[` usages exist.**
    86	
    87	> **Precision note (Codex round 2):** 648 is a *candidate* count from a uniform `pipeline-named-var = [` grep, not a hand-verified violation total. Codex's independent grep found 655 (or 605 requiring whitespace around `=`) — same ballpark. The large majority are genuine violations, but the pattern also catches a few *legitimate* cases: compliant inline calls split across lines, and deliberate list-of-pipelines reuse (e.g. `user_guide/pipelines/writing_pipelines.md:1242-1252`). Treat 648 as the upper-bound work-list for the sweep; the documented exceptions (below) carve out the legitimate ones.
    88	
    89	| Area | Violations | Notes |
    90	|---|---:|---|
    91	| `docs/source/user_guide/**` | **224** | epicenter of the how-to layer |
    92	| `examples/user/**` | 132 | the on-ramp the README points to |
    93	| `examples/developer/**` | 99 | branching/generator examples |
    94	| `docs/source/reference/**` | 69 | incl. `pipeline_syntax.md` (47), the canonical syntax page |
    95	| `docs/source/examples/**` (doc pages) | 42 | |
    96	| root `docs/source/*.md` (incl. `ai_onboarding.md` ×16) | 18 | |
    97	| `docs/source/getting_started/**` | 12 | the literal first tutorial |
    98	| `docs/source/concepts/**` | 12 | |
    99	| `docs/source/developer/**` | 10 | |
   100	| `docs/source/onboarding/**` | 7 | |
   101	| `examples/_internal`, `pipeline_samples`, `reference`, `aom_paper` | 23 | mostly non-user-facing tooling |
   102	
   103	**Worst single files:** `user_guide/pipelines/writing_pipelines.md` (51), `reference/pipeline_syntax.md` (47), `user_guide/pipelines/generators.md` (23), `user_guide/models/training.md` (20), `ai_onboarding.md` (16), `examples/user/03_preprocessing/U01_preprocessing_basics.py` (9).
   104	
   105	**Interpretation.** This is a *propagated template defect*, not isolated authoring lapses — the same `pipeline = [...]` skeleton was copied everywhere. That is good news for remediation: a single mechanical sweep clears the overwhelming majority. **But** a documented exception is warranted for two legitimate cases, and the proposal must name them so the pattern does not regenerate:
   106	- **Deliberate reuse / comparison** examples that run the *same* pipeline through several `run()` calls or `PipelineRunner`/`Session` deep-dives (a handful in `06_deployment`, `06_internals`).
   107	- **Synthesis/utility** scripts (`developer/02_generators/D05–D09`, `examples/_internal/*`) that are not pipeline tutorials.
   108	
   109	Even those should be re-examined; most can still be inlined. **A `ruff`/grep CI lint enforcing the inline form on `docs/` and `examples/` is the only durable fix** — without it, 648 becomes 700 by the next release.
   110

   178	
   179	## 5. Gap-closing pass (surfaces the fan-out missed)
   180	
   181	### 5.1 `examples/predictions.ipynb` — the single largest coverage hole
   182	
   183	A 1.8 MB Jupyter notebook ships as an example but is **referenced by no runner and no doc page**, and is executed by **no CI**. It is **stale and unrunnable** against 0.9.1:
   184	- `Predictions.load(path=…)` — **no such method**. `Predictions` has `from_workspace()` / `from_file()` / `from_parquet()` (`nirs4all/data/predictions.py:497,530,548`) and a path-detecting constructor.
   185	- `predictions._storage._df` — **no such attribute**. Internal state is `self._store` / `self._buffer` (`predictions.py:236,240`). The notebook reaches into a private Polars frame that doesn't exist.
   186	
   187	**Health 1/5.** Recommendation: either delete it, or rewrite as a runnable `examples/reference/R04_visualization.py` (conveniently filling the missing-R04 gap, #34) using the public `PredictionAnalyzer` API, and add it to `run_ci_examples.sh`. A shipped, un-CI'd, broken artifact is worse than no artifact.
   188	
   189	### 5.2 Hand-written `api/*.md` pages
   190	
   191	| Page | Health | Key issue |
   192	|---|---|---|
   193	| `api/module_api.md` | 3/5 | predict() doc names first param `source` (real `model`); 1 style violation. *(The `get_feature_importance()` "fake method" flagged by the reader is actually real — `result.py:1237`.)* |
   194	| `api/sklearn_integration.md` | 4/5 | clean; imports verified (`NIRSPipeline`, `NIRSPipelineClassifier` both exported) |
   195	| `api/storage.md` | 2/5 | "Version 5.0"; duplicates `reference/storage.md` (~800 vs ~400 LOC); legacy `runs/` framing |
   196	| `api/workspace.md` | 2/5 | missing "no `runs/`" principle; PipelineLibrary section 100% duplicate of `reference/workspace.md` |
   197	| `reference/api/session.md` | 4/5 | **orphaned** (no toctree); minor unverified property docs |
   198	
   199	**Pattern:** the `api/` tree (4 hand-written pages + 357 autodoc stubs) and the `reference/` tree document the same surface twice. This is a Phase-3 consolidation target: pick one API-reference home.
   200	
   201	### 5.3 Build / RTD hygiene — the root cause of undetected drift
   202	
   203	- **(A) Broken cross-refs are actively suppressed.** `conf.py` `nitpick_ignore_regex` blankets entire namespaces — `nirs4all.data.*`, `nirs4all.pipeline.*`, `nirs4all.api.*` — and `suppress_warnings` includes `myst.xref_missing` and `ref.*`. Any typo'd `:class:` ref in those namespaces is invisible. **And** CI `docs.yml` builds with `-W --keep-going` (strict) while `.readthedocs.yaml` sets `fail_on_warning: false` — CI and the published build disagree on strictness.
   204	- **(B) Asset integrity: clean.** All referenced images exist with alt text. 3 orphaned asset files (#39).
   205	- **(C) Zero doc-snippet execution.** No `doctest` / `nbval` / `myst_nb` / `literalinclude`-exec anywhere. The only executed code is `examples/*.py`, and `examples.yml` runs **weekly (cron Sunday) + manual only — never on push/PR** (the workflow header says so explicitly). This is *why* `result.predict()`, `bundle=`, `plot_predictions()`, `SklearnWrapper`, and the notebook's `Predictions.load()` all survived: nothing executes them, and the one thing that could runs once a week.
   206	
   207	**This is the highest-leverage systemic fix.** A doc-snippet execution gate (or at minimum moving `examples.yml` to per-PR for a fast subset) plus a tightened `nitpick_ignore` converts the entire class of wrong-API defects from "ships silently" to "fails the build."
   208	
   209	---
   210	
   211	## 6. Transparency: false positives caught and corrected
   212	
   213	To keep the register trustworthy, the audit's own mistakes are recorded rather than hidden (full reasoning in §1.1). The raw 22-agent pass produced ~216 candidate defects; the completeness critic + manual verification **downgraded 2 of the 9 raw "criticals"** (bare classes #21, transfer imports #20) and **corrected the headline style count** from "~250, 2 clean segments" to "~648 candidate sites, 0 clean segments."
   214	
   215	**Codex review round 2 (verdict: SOLID-WITH-FIXES; transcript `codex_reviews/phase2_audit_review.txt`)** independently spot-checked the register against source — confirming #3, #4, #5 scale (its grep: 605–655), #7, #9, #10, #12/#13/#15, #19 — and forced six accuracy fixes, all re-verified against source and applied above:
   216	
   217	1. **License is dual, not "CeCILL = wrong."** `LICENSE:1-13` = default AGPL-3.0-or-later + optional GPL-3.0/CeCILL-2.1 + commercial; `README:430-431` says so. Defect reframed (#1); the "ban CeCILL token" CI gate idea is removed.
   218	2. **`bundle=`** is absorbed by `**runner_kwargs` (no bind-time `TypeError`); fails the model/chain_id validation instead (#4).
   219	3. **`ExplainResult.get_feature_importance()` exists** (`result.py:1237`) — the reader's "fake method" subclaim was wrong; dropped (#22, §5.2).
   220	4. **`PredictionAnalyzer(result)`** is a second bug — constructor wants a `Predictions` (#9).
   221	5. **`target_column` is not a `DatasetConfigs` kwarg** — belongs in `global_params`; the `y_column→target_column` rename was wrong (#11).
   222	6. **Stale `Predictions.load()` also lives in `visualization/predictions.py:76` docstring** → autodoc inherits it (#14).
   223	
   224	Net: the register above is the trustworthy, twice-reviewed artifact; the per-segment JSON in `data/audit_segments.json` is raw input and still contains the un-pruned claims.

   249	| examples developer/01+02 | 2 | Comprehensive but ~heavy style violations, wrong-dir cross-refs. |
   250	| examples developer/03–06 | 2 | Wrong transfer import paths (guarded), heavy style, 2 demos never run. |
   251	| docs build config + RTD | 2 | Sound scripts; stale `conf.py` release/copyright; suppression masks broken refs. |
   252	
   253	**Mean: 2.80 / 5.**
   254	
   255	---
   256	
   257	## 8. What this means for Phase 3 (restructuring)
   258	
   259	The audit converges on a clear mandate for the restructuring proposal:
   260	
   261	1. **One canonical learning path, one source of truth per concept.** The single biggest *structural* defect is the 3–4 competing front doors (`getting_started/` vs `concepts/` vs `onboarding/` vs `ai_onboarding.md`) and the duplicated `api/` ↔ `reference/` trees. Phase 3 must pick a target information architecture (a Diátaxis-style split is the obvious candidate) and assign every existing page a home or a deletion.
   262	2. **The style mandate becomes infrastructure, not aspiration.** "1 pipeline inline + `run()`" must be enforced by a CI lint over `docs/` + `examples/`, with the two documented exceptions, or 648 will regrow.
   263	3. **Documentation must enter the safety net.** Per-PR execution of a fast example subset + a doc-snippet doctest gate + a tightened `nitpick_ignore`. This is what makes the rewrite *stay* correct.
   264	4. **Metadata is sourced from one place.** Version/license/copyright derived from `nirs4all.__version__` and `LICENSE`, with a CI grep gate.
   265	
   266	Phase 3 will deliver the target IA, a page-by-page migration map (keep / merge / rewrite / delete), the enforced style guide, and the CI gates — justified against these findings.
   267	
   268	---
   269	
   270	### Appendix — raw data & reproducibility
   271	
   272	- `GROUND_TRUTH.md` — the source-verified API surface every agent grounded against.
   273	- `data/audit_segments.json` — 20 raw segment reports (un-pruned; contains the false positives corrected in §6).
   274	- `data/audit_synthesis.json` — cross-cutting synthesis (raw).
   275	- `data/audit_completeness_critic.json` — adversarial critic output.
   276	- `audit_workflow.js` — the workflow script (re-runnable / resumable).
   277	- Authoritative style count reproducible via the grep in §3 (variable-name-contains-`pipeline`, list-literal assignment, over `docs/source/**.md` + `examples/**.py`).

     2	NIRS4All - A comprehensive package for Near-Infrared Spectroscopy data processing and analysis.
     3	
     4	This package provides tools for spectroscopy data handling, preprocessing, model building,
     5	and pipeline management with support for multiple ML backends.
     6	
     7	Public API (recommended)::
     8	
     9	    nirs4all.run(pipeline, dataset, ...)         - Train a pipeline
    10	    nirs4all.predict(model, data, ...)           - Make predictions
    11	    nirs4all.explain(model, data, ...)           - Generate SHAP explanations
    12	    nirs4all.retrain(source, data, ...)          - Retrain a pipeline
    13	    nirs4all.session(...)                        - Create execution session
    14	    nirs4all.load_session(path)                  - Load saved session
    15	    nirs4all.generate(n_samples, ...)            - Generate synthetic NIRS data
    16	
    17	Classes (for advanced usage):
    18	    nirs4all.PipelineRunner    - Direct runner access
    19	    nirs4all.PipelineConfigs   - Pipeline configuration
    20	    nirs4all.DatasetConfigs    - Dataset configuration (from nirs4all.data)
    21	
    22	Example:
    23	    >>> import nirs4all
    24	    >>> from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
    25	    >>> from sklearn.cross_decomposition import PLSRegression
    26	    >>>
    27	    >>> result = nirs4all.run(

/bin/bash -lc 'nl -ba nirs4all/api/run.py' in /home/delete/nirs4all/nirs4all
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	"""
     2	Module-level run() function for nirs4all.
     3	
     4	This module provides the primary entry point for training ML pipelines on NIRS data.
     5	It wraps PipelineRunner.run() with a simpler, more ergonomic interface.
     6	
     7	Example:
     8	    >>> import nirs4all
     9	    >>> result = nirs4all.run(
    10	    ...     pipeline=[MinMaxScaler(), PLSRegression(10)],
    11	    ...     dataset="sample_data/regression",
    12	    ...     verbose=1
    13	    ... )
    14	    >>> print(f"Best RMSE: {result.best_rmse:.4f}")
    15	"""
    16	
    17	from pathlib import Path
    18	from typing import Any, TypeAlias
    19	
    20	import numpy as np
    21	
    22	from nirs4all.config.cache_config import CacheConfig
    23	from nirs4all.data import DatasetConfigs
    24	from nirs4all.data.dataset import SpectroDataset
    25	from nirs4all.data.predictions import Predictions
    26	from nirs4all.pipeline import PipelineConfigs, PipelineRunner
    27	
    28	from .result import RunResult
    29	from .session import Session
    30	
    31	# Type aliases for a single pipeline or dataset (not lists)
    32	SinglePipelineSpec: TypeAlias = (
    33	    list[Any]                    # List of steps (most common)
    34	    | dict[str, Any]               # Dict configuration
    35	    | str                          # Path to YAML/JSON config
    36	    | Path                         # Path to config file
    37	    | PipelineConfigs               # Backward compat: existing PipelineConfigs
    38	)
    39	
    40	SingleDatasetSpec: TypeAlias = (
    41	    str                          # Path to data folder
    42	    | Path                         # Path to data folder
    43	    | np.ndarray                   # X array (y inferred or None)
    44	    | tuple[np.ndarray, ...]       # (X,) or (X, y) or (X, y, metadata)
    45	    | dict[str, Any]               # Dict with X, y, metadata keys
    46	    | SpectroDataset               # Direct SpectroDataset instance
    47	    | DatasetConfigs               # Backward compat: existing DatasetConfigs
    48	)
    49	
    50	# Type aliases that also support lists for batch execution
    51	PipelineSpec: TypeAlias = (
    52	    SinglePipelineSpec
    53	    | list[SinglePipelineSpec]     # List of pipelines for batch execution
    54	)
    55	
    56	DatasetSpec: TypeAlias = (
    57	    SingleDatasetSpec
    58	    | list[SingleDatasetSpec]      # List of datasets for batch execution
    59	)
    60	
    61	def _is_pipeline_wrapper_dict(obj: Any) -> bool:
    62	    """Return True for dicts that wrap a full pipeline definition."""
    63	    return isinstance(obj, dict) and any(key in obj for key in ("pipeline", "steps"))
    64	
    65	def _is_batch_pipeline_list(pipeline: list[Any]) -> bool:
    66	    """Return True only when every outer item is clearly a full pipeline spec.
    67	
    68	    This prevents nested canonical steps such as ``[[...], {...}]`` from being
    69	    misread as a batch of pipelines when they are actually one pipeline with a
    70	    nested list step followed by ordinary steps.
    71	    """
    72	    if not pipeline:
    73	        return False
    74	
    75	    saw_pipeline_spec = False
    76	    for item in pipeline:
    77	        if isinstance(item, (PipelineConfigs, str, Path)):
    78	            saw_pipeline_spec = True
    79	            continue
    80	        if isinstance(item, list):
    81	            saw_pipeline_spec = True
    82	            continue
    83	        if _is_pipeline_wrapper_dict(item):
    84	            saw_pipeline_spec = True
    85	            continue
    86	        if isinstance(item, dict) or _looks_like_step(item):
    87	            return False
    88	        return False
    89	
    90	    return saw_pipeline_spec
    91	
    92	def _is_single_pipeline(pipeline: Any) -> bool:
    93	    """Check if pipeline is a single pipeline definition (not a list of pipelines).
    94	
    95	    A single pipeline can be:
    96	    - A PipelineConfigs object
    97	    - A dict (configuration)
    98	    - A str/Path (config file path)
    99	    - A list of steps where steps are NOT themselves lists of steps
   100	
   101	    A list of pipelines would be:
   102	    - A list where elements are themselves lists of steps (each inner list is a pipeline)
   103	    """
   104	    if isinstance(pipeline, (PipelineConfigs, dict, str, Path)):
   105	        return True
   106	
   107	    if isinstance(pipeline, list):
   108	        if len(pipeline) == 0:
   109	            return True  # Empty list treated as single empty pipeline
   110	        return not _is_batch_pipeline_list(pipeline)
   111	
   112	    return True
   113	
   114	def _looks_like_step(obj: Any) -> bool:
   115	    """Check if an object looks like a pipeline step.
   116	
   117	    Steps can be:
   118	    - sklearn-like objects (have fit/transform/predict methods)
   119	    - Class objects (types)
   120	    - Dicts with step configuration keys
   121	    - None (no-op step)
   122	    """
   123	    if obj is None:
   124	        return True
   125	    if isinstance(obj, type):
   126	        return True  # It's a class
   127	    if isinstance(obj, dict):
   128	        return True
   129	    # Check if it's an instance with sklearn-like interface
   130	    if hasattr(obj, 'fit') or hasattr(obj, 'transform') or hasattr(obj, 'predict'):
   131	        return True
   132	    # Check for nirs4all transforms
   133	    return bool(hasattr(obj, '__class__') and obj.__class__.__module__.startswith('nirs4all'))
   134	
   135	def _is_single_dataset(dataset: Any) -> bool:
   136	    """Check if dataset is a single dataset definition (not a list of datasets).
   137	
   138	    A single dataset can be:
   139	    - A DatasetConfigs object
   140	    - A SpectroDataset instance
   141	    - A str/Path (data folder path)
   142	    - A numpy array
   143	    - A tuple of arrays (X, y, ...)
   144	    - A dict with X, y keys
   145	
   146	    A list of datasets would be:
   147	    - A list where each element is a dataset spec (str, SpectroDataset, dict, array, tuple)
   148	    """
   149	    if isinstance(dataset, (DatasetConfigs, SpectroDataset, str, Path, np.ndarray, tuple)):
   150	        return True
   151	
   152	    if isinstance(dataset, dict):
   153	        # A dict could be a dataset config or data dict
   154	        # If it has 'X' or 'features' key, it's a data dict (single dataset)
   155	        # Otherwise it could be a DatasetConfigs-like dict
   156	        return True
   157	
   158	    if isinstance(dataset, list):
   159	        if len(dataset) == 0:
   160	            return True  # Empty list treated as single empty dataset
   161	
   162	        first = dataset[0]
   163	
   164	        # List of SpectroDataset is treated as multi-dataset (handled specially by orchestrator)
   165	        if isinstance(first, SpectroDataset):
   166	            return False
   167	
   168	        # List of paths/strings -> multi-dataset
   169	        if isinstance(first, (str, Path)):
   170	            return False
   171	
   172	        # List of dicts where each dict is a dataset config -> multi-dataset
   173	        if isinstance(first, dict) and ('path' in first or 'X' in first or 'features' in first):
   174	            return False
   175	
   176	        # List of arrays or tuples -> multi-dataset
   177	        return not isinstance(first, (np.ndarray, tuple))
   178	
   179	    return True
   180	
   181	def _normalize_to_list(spec: Any, is_single_fn) -> list[Any]:
   182	    """Normalize a spec (pipeline or dataset) to a list of specs.
   183	
   184	    If it's a single spec, wrap it in a list.
   185	    If it's already a list of specs, return as-is.
   186	    """
   187	    if is_single_fn(spec):
   188	        return [spec]
   189	    else:
   190	        return list(spec)
   191	
   192	def run(
   193	    pipeline: PipelineSpec,
   194	    dataset: DatasetSpec,
   195	    *,
   196	    name: str = "",
   197	    session: Session | None = None,
   198	    # Common runner options (shortcuts for most-used parameters)
   199	    verbose: int = 1,
   200	    save_artifacts: bool = True,
   201	    save_charts: bool = True,
   202	    plots_visible: bool = False,
   203	    random_state: int | None = None,
   204	    refit: bool | dict[str, Any] | list[dict[str, Any]] | None = True,
   205	    cache: Any | None = None,
   206	    project: str | None = None,
   207	    report_naming: str = "nirs",
   208	    # All other PipelineRunner options
   209	    **runner_kwargs: Any
   210	) -> RunResult:
   211	    """Execute a training pipeline on a dataset.
   212	
   213	    This is the primary entry point for training ML pipelines on NIRS data.
   214	    It provides a simpler interface than creating PipelineRunner and config
   215	    objects directly.
   216	
   217	    Args:
   218	        pipeline: Pipeline definition. Can be:
   219	            - List of steps (most common): ``[MinMaxScaler(), PLSRegression(10)]``
   220	            - Dict with steps: ``{"steps": [...], "name": "my_pipeline"}``
   221	            - Path to YAML/JSON config file: ``"configs/my_pipeline.yaml"``
   222	            - PipelineConfigs object (backward compatibility)
   223	            - **List of pipelines**: ``[pipeline1, pipeline2, ...]`` - each
   224	              pipeline is executed independently (cartesian product with datasets)
   225	
   226	        dataset: Dataset definition. Can be:
   227	            - Path to data folder: ``"sample_data/regression"``
   228	            - Numpy arrays: ``(X, y)`` or ``X`` alone
   229	            - Dict with arrays: ``{"X": X, "y": y, "metadata": meta}``
   230	            - SpectroDataset instance
   231	            - List of SpectroDataset instances (multi-dataset)
   232	            - DatasetConfigs object (backward compatibility)
   233	            - **List of datasets**: ``[dataset1, dataset2, ...]`` - each
   234	              dataset is used with each pipeline (cartesian product)
   235	
   236	        name: Optional pipeline name for identification and logging.
   237	            If not provided, a name will be generated.
   238	
   239	        session: Optional Session object for resource reuse across multiple
   240	            runs. When provided, shares workspace and configuration.
   241	
   242	        verbose: Verbosity level (0=quiet, 1=info, 2=debug, 3=trace).
   243	            Default: 1
   244	
   245	        save_artifacts: Whether to save binary artifacts (models, transformers).
   246	            Default: True
   247	
   248	        save_charts: Whether to save charts and visual outputs.
   249	            Default: True
   250	
   251	        plots_visible: Whether to display plots interactively.
   252	            Default: False
   253	
   254	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   255	            Default: None (no seeding)
   256	
   257	        refit: Refit configuration. After cross-validation selects the
   258	            winning pipeline variant(s), retrain on the full training set.
   259	            - ``True``: Refit top 1 by RMSECV (default).
   260	            - ``False`` or ``None``: Disable refit.
   261	            - ``dict``: Single criterion, e.g. ``{"top_k": 3, "ranking": "mean_val"}``.
   262	            - ``list[dict]``: Multiple criteria for union selection, e.g.
   263	              ``[{"top_k": 3, "ranking": "rmsecv"}, {"top_k": 1, "ranking": "mean_val"}]``.
   264	            Ranking methods: ``"rmsecv"`` (OOF concatenated val score),
   265	            ``"mean_val"`` (mean of individual fold val scores).
   266	
   267	        cache: Optional CacheConfig for step-level caching.
   268	            - ``None``: Use default CacheConfig (step cache OFF, CoW snapshots ON).
   269	            - ``CacheConfig(step_cache_enabled=True)``: Enable step caching.
   270	
   271	        project: Optional project name to tag the run with.  If the project
   272	            does not exist yet it will be created automatically.
   273	
   274	        report_naming: Naming convention for metrics in reports and summaries.
   275	            - ``"nirs"`` (default): Chemometrics terminology (RMSECV, RMSEP, etc.)
   276	            - ``"ml"``: Machine learning terminology (CV_Score, Test_Score, etc.)
   277	            - ``"auto"``: Auto-detect based on context (defaults to "nirs")
   278	            Affects column headers in final summary tables. Internal variable names
   279	            use ML conventions regardless of this setting.
   280	
   281	        **runner_kwargs: Additional PipelineRunner parameters. See
   282	            PipelineRunner.__init__ for full list. Common options:
   283	            - workspace_path: Workspace root directory
   284	            - continue_on_error: Whether to continue on step failures
   285	            - show_spinner: Whether to show progress spinners
   286	            - log_file: Whether to write logs to disk
   287	            - log_format: Output format ("pretty", "minimal", "json")
   288	            - show_progress_bar: Whether to show progress bars
   289	            - max_generation_count: Max pipeline combinations (for generators)
   290	
   291	    Returns:
   292	        RunResult containing:
   293	            - predictions: Predictions object with all pipeline results
   294	            - per_dataset: Dictionary with per-dataset execution details
   295	            - best: Best prediction entry (convenience accessor)
   296	            - best_score: Best model's primary test score
   297	            - best_rmse, best_r2, best_accuracy: Score shortcuts
   298	
   299	        Use ``result.top(n=5)`` to get top N predictions, or
   300	        ``result.export("path.n4a")`` to export the best model.
   301	
   302	    Raises:
   303	        ValueError: If pipeline or dataset format is invalid.
   304	        FileNotFoundError: If pipeline config or dataset path doesn't exist.
   305	
   306	    Examples:
   307	        Simple usage with list of steps:
   308	
   309	        >>> import nirs4all
   310	        >>> from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
   311	        >>> from sklearn.cross_decomposition import PLSRegression
   312	        >>>
   313	        >>> result = nirs4all.run(
   314	        ...     pipeline=[MinMaxScaler(), PLSRegression(10)],
   315	        ...     dataset="sample_data/regression",
   316	        ...     verbose=1
   317	        ... )
   318	        >>> print(f"Best RMSE: {result.best_rmse:.4f}")
   319	
   320	        With cross-validation and multiple models:
   321	
   322	        >>> from sklearn.model_selection import ShuffleSplit
   323	        >>>
   324	        >>> result = nirs4all.run(
   325	        ...     pipeline=[
   326	        ...         MinMaxScaler(),
   327	        ...         ShuffleSplit(n_splits=3),
   328	        ...         {"model": PLSRegression(10)}
   329	        ...     ],
   330	        ...     dataset="sample_data/regression",
   331	        ...     name="PLS_experiment",
   332	        ...     verbose=2,
   333	        ...     save_artifacts=True
   334	        ... )
   335	
   336	        Multiple pipelines executed independently:
   337	
   338	        >>> pipeline_pls = [MinMaxScaler(), PLSRegression(10)]
   339	        >>> pipeline_rf = [StandardScaler(), RandomForestRegressor()]
   340	        >>>
   341	        >>> result = nirs4all.run(
   342	        ...     pipeline=[pipeline_pls, pipeline_rf],  # Two independent pipelines
   343	        ...     dataset="sample_data/regression",
   344	        ...     verbose=1
   345	        ... )
   346	        >>> print(f"Total configs: {result.num_predictions}")
   347	
   348	        Cartesian product of pipelines × datasets:
   349	
   350	        >>> pipelines = [pipeline1, pipeline2, pipeline3]
   351	        >>> datasets = [dataset_a, dataset_b]
   352	        >>>
   353	        >>> # Runs 6 combinations: p1×da, p1×db, p2×da, p2×db, p3×da, p3×db
   354	        >>> result = nirs4all.run(
   355	        ...     pipeline=pipelines,
   356	        ...     dataset=datasets,
   357	        ...     verbose=1
   358	        ... )
   359	
   360	        Using a session for multiple runs:
   361	
   362	        >>> with nirs4all.session(verbose=1) as s:
   363	        ...     r1 = nirs4all.run(pipeline1, data, session=s)
   364	        ...     r2 = nirs4all.run(pipeline2, data, session=s)
   365	        ...     print(f"Pipeline 1: {r1.best_score:.4f}")
   366	        ...     print(f"Pipeline 2: {r2.best_score:.4f}")
   367	
   368	        Export the best model:
   369	
   370	        >>> result = nirs4all.run(pipeline, dataset)
   371	        >>> result.export("exports/best_model.n4a")
   372	
   373	    See Also:
   374	        - :func:`nirs4all.predict`: Make predictions with a trained model
   375	        - :func:`nirs4all.explain`: Generate SHAP explanations
   376	        - :func:`nirs4all.session`: Create execution session for resource reuse
   377	        - :class:`nirs4all.PipelineRunner`: Direct runner access for advanced use
   378	    """
   379	    # Normalize pipelines and datasets to lists
   380	    pipelines = _normalize_to_list(pipeline, _is_single_pipeline)
   381	    datasets = _normalize_to_list(dataset, _is_single_dataset)
   382	
   383	    # Extract store_run_id before passing runner_kwargs to PipelineRunner
   384	    caller_store_run_id: str | None = runner_kwargs.pop("store_run_id", None)
   385	
   386	    # If session provided, use its runner
   387	    if session is not None:
   388	        runner = session.runner
   389	        # Update runner settings if explicitly provided
   390	        if verbose != 1:  # Not the default
   391	            runner.verbose = verbose
   392	    else:
   393	        # Build runner kwargs from explicit params + extras
   394	        all_kwargs = {
   395	            "verbose": verbose,
   396	            "save_artifacts": save_artifacts,
   397	            "save_charts": save_charts,
   398	            "plots_visible": plots_visible,
   399	            "report_naming": report_naming,
   400	            **runner_kwargs
   401	        }
   402	        if random_state is not None:
   403	            all_kwargs["random_state"] = random_state
   404	
   405	        runner = PipelineRunner(**all_kwargs)
   406	
   407	    # Set cache config on runner (flows to orchestrator -> runtime_context).
   408	    # Default path keeps step cache disabled while enabling CoW snapshots.
   409	    runner.cache_config = cache if cache is not None else CacheConfig()
   410	
   411	    # Execute the cartesian product: each pipeline × each dataset
   412	    all_predictions = Predictions()
   413	    all_per_dataset: dict[str, Any] = {}
   414	    total_combos = len(pipelines) * len(datasets)
   415	
   416	    # When multiple combos or caller provided a store_run_id, group all
   417	    # pipeline×dataset executions under a single store run.
   418	    shared_run_id: str | None = caller_store_run_id
   419	    caller_owns_run = caller_store_run_id is not None  # Caller manages lifecycle
   420	    multi_run = total_combos > 1 or shared_run_id is not None
   421	
   422	    if multi_run and shared_run_id is None:
   423	        # Pre-create a single store run for the whole batch
   424	        store = getattr(runner, 'orchestrator', runner).store if hasattr(runner, 'orchestrator') else None
   425	        if store is None:
   426	            store = getattr(getattr(runner, 'orchestrator', None), 'store', None)
   427	        if store is not None and hasattr(store, 'begin_run'):
   428	            import json as _json
   429	            dataset_meta = []
   430	            for ds in datasets:
   431	                if isinstance(ds, str):
   432	                    dataset_meta.append({"name": Path(ds).stem})
   433	                elif hasattr(ds, 'name'):
   434	                    dataset_meta.append({"name": ds.name})
   435	                else:
   436	                    dataset_meta.append({"name": "dataset"})
   437	            shared_run_id = store.begin_run(
   438	                name=name or "run",
   439	                config={"n_pipelines": len(pipelines), "n_datasets": len(datasets)},
   440	                datasets=dataset_meta,
   441	            )
   442	
   443	    try:
   444	        for pipeline_idx, single_pipeline in enumerate(pipelines):
   445	            for _dataset_idx, single_dataset in enumerate(datasets):
   446	                # Generate name with index if multiple pipelines
   447	                pipeline_name = f"{name}_p{pipeline_idx}" if name else f"pipeline_{pipeline_idx}" if len(pipelines) > 1 else name
   448	
   449	                # Convert Path to str for compatibility with type hints
   450	                pipeline_arg = str(single_pipeline) if isinstance(single_pipeline, Path) else single_pipeline
   451	                dataset_arg = str(single_dataset) if isinstance(single_dataset, Path) else single_dataset
   452	
   453	                predictions, per_dataset = runner.run(
   454	                    pipeline=pipeline_arg,
   455	                    dataset=dataset_arg,
   456	                    pipeline_name=pipeline_name,
   457	                    refit=refit,
   458	                    store_run_id=shared_run_id,
   459	                    manage_store_run=not multi_run,
   460	                )
   461	
   462	                # Merge predictions from this run
   463	                all_predictions.merge_predictions(predictions)
   464	
   465	                # Merge per_dataset info (datasets with same name will be combined)
   466	                for ds_name, ds_info in per_dataset.items():
   467	                    if ds_name not in all_per_dataset:
   468	                        all_per_dataset[ds_name] = ds_info
   469	                    else:
   470	                        # Merge run_predictions from multiple runs on same dataset
   471	                        existing_run_preds = all_per_dataset[ds_name].get("run_predictions")
   472	                        new_run_preds = ds_info.get("run_predictions")
   473	                        if existing_run_preds is not None and new_run_preds is not None:
   474	                            existing_run_preds.merge_predictions(new_run_preds)
   475	
   476	        # Complete the shared store run (only if we created it, not if caller owns it)
   477	        if multi_run and shared_run_id is not None and not caller_owns_run:
   478	            store = getattr(getattr(runner, 'orchestrator', None), 'store', None)
   479	            if store is not None and hasattr(store, 'complete_run'):
   480	                summary: dict[str, Any] = {"total_pipelines": total_combos}
   481	                if all_predictions.num_predictions > 0:
   482	                    best = all_predictions.get_best(ascending=None, score_scope="all")
   483	                    if best:
   484	                        summary["best_score"] = best.get("test_score")
   485	                        summary["best_metric"] = best.get("metric")
   486	                store.complete_run(shared_run_id, summary)
   487	
   488	    except Exception as e:
   489	        # Fail the shared store run (only if we created it)
   490	        if multi_run and shared_run_id is not None and not caller_owns_run:
   491	            store = getattr(getattr(runner, 'orchestrator', None), 'store', None)
   492	            if store is not None and hasattr(store, 'fail_run'):
   493	                store.fail_run(shared_run_id, str(e))
   494	        raise
   495	
   496	    # Extract per-model selections from the orchestrator (if available)
   497	    orchestrator = getattr(runner, 'orchestrator', None)
   498	    per_model_selections = getattr(orchestrator, '_per_model_selections', None) if orchestrator else None
   499	
   500	    # Tag the run with a project if requested
   501	    if project is not None and orchestrator is not None:
   502	        run_id = shared_run_id or getattr(orchestrator, 'last_run_id', None)
   503	        store = getattr(orchestrator, 'store', None)
   504	        if run_id and store and hasattr(store, 'get_or_create_project'):
   505	            project_id = store.get_or_create_project(project)
   506	            store.set_run_project(run_id, project_id)
   507	
   508	    result = RunResult(
   509	        predictions=all_predictions,
   510	        per_dataset=all_per_dataset,
   511	        _runner=runner,
   512	        _owns_runner=session is None,
   513	        _workspace_path=runner.workspace_path,
   514	        _per_model_selections=per_model_selections,
   515	    )
   516	
   517	    # For non-session runs, detach from the runner immediately to release
   518	    # the DB connection.  Export operations will re-open the store on demand.
   519	    if session is None:
   520	        result.detach()
   521	
   522	    return result
