/bin/bash -lc 'nl -ba nirs4all/api/generate.py' in /home/delete/nirs4all/nirs4all
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	"""
     2	Top-level generate() API for synthetic NIRS data generation.
     3	
     4	This module provides the primary entry points for generating synthetic
     5	NIRS datasets within nirs4all.
     6	
     7	Example:
     8	    >>> import nirs4all
     9	    >>>
    10	    >>> # Simple generation
    11	    >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate(n_samples=1000, random_state=42)
    12	    >>>
    13	    >>> # Convenience functions
    14	    >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.regression(n_samples=500)
    15	    >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.classification(n_samples=300, n_classes=3)
    16	    >>>
    17	    >>> # Builder access
    18	    >>> builder = nirs4all.generate.builder(n_samples=1000)
    19	"""
    20	
    21	from __future__ import annotations
    22	
    23	import contextlib
    24	from typing import TYPE_CHECKING, Any, Literal, Optional, Union, overload
    25	
    26	import numpy as np
    27	
    28	if TYPE_CHECKING:
    29	    from pathlib import Path
    30	
    31	    from nirs4all.data.dataset import SpectroDataset
    32	    from nirs4all.synthesis import SyntheticDatasetBuilder
    33	
    34	@overload
    35	def generate(
    36	    n_samples: int = ...,
    37	    *,
    38	    random_state: int | None = ...,
    39	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
    40	    wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
    41	    components: list[str] | None = ...,
    42	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
    43	    train_ratio: float = ...,
    44	    as_dataset: Literal[True] = ...,
    45	    name: str = ...,
    46	    **kwargs: Any,
    47	) -> SpectroDataset: ...
    48	
    49	@overload
    50	def generate(
    51	    n_samples: int = ...,
    52	    *,
    53	    random_state: int | None = ...,
    54	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
    55	    wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
    56	    components: list[str] | None = ...,
    57	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
    58	    train_ratio: float = ...,
    59	    as_dataset: Literal[False],
    60	    name: str = ...,
    61	    **kwargs: Any,
    62	) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]: ...
    63	
    64	def generate(
    65	    n_samples: int = 1000,
    66	    *,
    67	    random_state: int | None = None,
    68	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "simple",
    69	    wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
    70	    components: list[str] | None = None,
    71	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
    72	    train_ratio: float = 0.8,
    73	    as_dataset: bool = True,
    74	    name: str = "synthetic_nirs",
    75	    **kwargs: Any,
    76	) -> SpectroDataset | tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
    77	    """
    78	    Generate a synthetic NIRS dataset.
    79	
    80	    This is the primary function for creating synthetic spectroscopic data.
    81	    It provides a simple interface for common use cases while allowing
    82	    full customization through keyword arguments.
    83	
    84	    Args:
    85	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
    86	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
    87	        complexity: Complexity level affecting noise, scatter, etc.
    88	            Options: 'simple' (fast, minimal noise), 'realistic' (typical NIR),
    89	            'complex' (challenging scenarios).
    90	        wavelength_range: Tuple of (start, end) wavelengths in nm.
    91	            Defaults to (1000, 2500) which covers the full NIR range.
    92	        components: List of predefined component names to use.
    93	            Options: 'water', 'protein', 'lipid', 'starch', 'cellulose',
    94	            'chlorophyll', 'oil', 'nitrogen_compound'.
    95	        target_range: Optional (min, max) range for scaling targets.
    96	        train_ratio: Proportion of samples for training partition.
    97	        as_dataset: If True, returns SpectroDataset. If False, returns (X, y) tuple.
    98	        name: Dataset name.
    99	        **kwargs: Additional arguments passed to SyntheticDatasetBuilder.
   100	
   101	    Returns:
   102	        If as_dataset=True: SpectroDataset ready for pipeline use.
   103	        If as_dataset=False: Tuple of (X, y) numpy arrays.
   104	
   105	    Example:
   106	        >>> import nirs4all
   107	        >>>
   108	        >>> # Basic usage
   109	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate(n_samples=1000, random_state=42)
   110	        >>>
   111	        >>> # Quick arrays for prototyping
   112	        >>> X, y = nirs4all.generate(n_samples=500, as_dataset=False)
   113	        >>>
   114	        >>> # Realistic spectra
   115	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate(
   116	        ...     n_samples=1000,
   117	        ...     complexity="realistic",
   118	        ...     components=["water", "protein", "lipid"],
   119	        ...     target_range=(0, 100),
   120	        ...     random_state=42
   121	        ... )
   122	
   123	    See Also:
   124	        generate.regression: Convenience function for regression datasets.
   125	        generate.classification: Convenience function for classification datasets.
   126	        generate.builder: Access the full builder API.
   127	    """
   128	    from nirs4all.synthesis import SyntheticDatasetBuilder
   129	
   130	    builder = SyntheticDatasetBuilder(
   131	        n_samples=n_samples,
   132	        random_state=random_state,
   133	        name=name,
   134	    )
   135	
   136	    # Configure features
   137	    feature_kwargs: dict[str, Any] = {"complexity": complexity}
   138	    if wavelength_range is not None:
   139	        feature_kwargs["wavelength_range"] = wavelength_range
   140	    if components is not None:
   141	        feature_kwargs["components"] = components
   142	
   143	    builder.with_features(**feature_kwargs)
   144	
   145	    # Configure targets
   146	    if target_range is not None:
   147	        builder.with_targets(range=target_range)
   148	
   149	    # Configure partitions
   150	    builder.with_partitions(train_ratio=train_ratio)
   151	
   152	    # Configure output
   153	    builder.with_output(as_dataset=as_dataset)
   154	
   155	    # Handle additional kwargs for advanced configuration
   156	    if "distribution" in kwargs:
   157	        builder.with_targets(distribution=kwargs.pop("distribution"))
   158	
   159	    if "batch_effects" in kwargs:
   160	        builder.with_batch_effects(enabled=kwargs.pop("batch_effects"))
   161	
   162	    return builder.build()
   163	
   164	@overload
   165	def regression(
   166	    n_samples: int = ...,
   167	    *,
   168	    random_state: int | None = ...,
   169	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
   170	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
   171	    target_component: str | int | None = ...,
   172	    distribution: Literal["dirichlet", "uniform", "lognormal", "correlated"] = ...,
   173	    train_ratio: float = ...,
   174	    as_dataset: Literal[True] = ...,
   175	    name: str = ...,
   176	) -> SpectroDataset: ...
   177	
   178	@overload
   179	def regression(
   180	    n_samples: int = ...,
   181	    *,
   182	    random_state: int | None = ...,
   183	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
   184	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
   185	    target_component: str | int | None = ...,
   186	    distribution: Literal["dirichlet", "uniform", "lognormal", "correlated"] = ...,
   187	    train_ratio: float = ...,
   188	    as_dataset: Literal[False],
   189	    name: str = ...,
   190	) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]: ...
   191	
   192	def regression(
   193	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   194	    *,
   195	    random_state: int | None = None,
   196	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "simple",
   197	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   198	    target_component: str | int | None = None,
   199	    distribution: Literal["dirichlet", "uniform", "lognormal", "correlated"] = "dirichlet",
   200	    train_ratio: float = 0.8,
   201	    as_dataset: bool = True,
   202	    name: str = "synthetic_regression",
   203	) -> SpectroDataset | tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
   204	    """
   205	    Generate a synthetic NIRS dataset for regression tasks.
   206	
   207	    This convenience function is optimized for regression scenarios,
   208	    with sensible defaults for target distribution and scaling.
   209	
   210	    Args:
   211	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   212	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   213	        complexity: Complexity level ('simple', 'realistic', 'complex').
   214	        target_range: Target value range (min, max) for scaling.
   215	        target_component: Which component to use as target.
   216	            If None, uses all components (multi-output regression).
   217	        distribution: Concentration distribution method.
   218	        train_ratio: Proportion of samples for training partition.
   219	        as_dataset: If True, returns SpectroDataset. If False, returns (X, y).
   220	        name: Dataset name.
   221	
   222	    Returns:
   223	        If as_dataset=True: SpectroDataset ready for pipeline use.
   224	        If as_dataset=False: Tuple of (X, y) numpy arrays.
   225	
   226	    Example:
   227	        >>> import nirs4all
   228	        >>>
   229	        >>> # Simple regression dataset
   230	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.regression(n_samples=500)
   231	        >>>
   232	        >>> # Single target with scaling
   233	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.regression(
   234	        ...     n_samples=1000,
   235	        ...     target_range=(0, 100),
   236	        ...     target_component="protein",
   237	        ...     random_state=42
   238	        ... )
   239	    """
   240	    from nirs4all.synthesis import SyntheticDatasetBuilder
   241	
   242	    builder = SyntheticDatasetBuilder(
   243	        n_samples=n_samples,
   244	        random_state=random_state,
   245	        name=name,
   246	    )
   247	
   248	    builder.with_features(complexity=complexity)
   249	
   250	    target_kwargs: dict[str, Any] = {"distribution": distribution}
   251	    if target_range is not None:
   252	        target_kwargs["range"] = target_range
   253	    if target_component is not None:
   254	        target_kwargs["component"] = target_component
   255	
   256	    builder.with_targets(**target_kwargs)
   257	    builder.with_partitions(train_ratio=train_ratio)
   258	    builder.with_output(as_dataset=as_dataset)
   259	
   260	    return builder.build()
   261	
   262	@overload
   263	def classification(
   264	    n_samples: int = ...,
   265	    *,
   266	    n_classes: int = ...,
   267	    random_state: int | None = ...,
   268	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
   269	    class_separation: float = ...,
   270	    class_weights: list[float] | None = ...,
   271	    train_ratio: float = ...,
   272	    as_dataset: Literal[True] = ...,
   273	    name: str = ...,
   274	) -> SpectroDataset: ...
   275	
   276	@overload
   277	def classification(
   278	    n_samples: int = ...,
   279	    *,
   280	    n_classes: int = ...,
   281	    random_state: int | None = ...,
   282	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
   283	    class_separation: float = ...,
   284	    class_weights: list[float] | None = ...,
   285	    train_ratio: float = ...,
   286	    as_dataset: Literal[False],
   287	    name: str = ...,
   288	) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]: ...
   289	
   290	def classification(
   291	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   292	    *,
   293	    n_classes: int = 2,
   294	    random_state: int | None = None,
   295	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "simple",
   296	    class_separation: float = 1.0,
   297	    class_weights: list[float] | None = None,
   298	    train_ratio: float = 0.8,
   299	    as_dataset: bool = True,
   300	    name: str = "synthetic_classification",
   301	) -> SpectroDataset | tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
   302	    """
   303	    Generate a synthetic NIRS dataset for classification tasks.
   304	
   305	    This convenience function creates datasets with discrete class labels,
   306	    suitable for classification experiments.
   307	
   308	    Args:
   309	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   310	        n_classes: Number of classes (2 for binary, >2 for multiclass).
   311	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   312	        complexity: Complexity level ('simple', 'realistic', 'complex').
   313	        class_separation: Separation factor between classes.
   314	            Higher values make classes more distinguishable.
   315	        class_weights: Optional class proportions for imbalanced datasets.
   316	            Should sum to 1.0.
   317	        train_ratio: Proportion of samples for training partition.
   318	        as_dataset: If True, returns SpectroDataset. If False, returns (X, y).
   319	        name: Dataset name.
   320	
   321	    Returns:
   322	        If as_dataset=True: SpectroDataset ready for pipeline use.
   323	        If as_dataset=False: Tuple of (X, y) numpy arrays where y is integer labels.
   324	
   325	    Example:
   326	        >>> import nirs4all
   327	        >>>
   328	        >>> # Binary classification
   329	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.classification(n_samples=500, n_classes=2)
   330	        >>>
   331	        >>> # Multiclass with imbalanced classes
   332	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.classification(
   333	        ...     n_samples=1000,
   334	        ...     n_classes=3,
   335	        ...     class_weights=[0.5, 0.3, 0.2],
   336	        ...     random_state=42
   337	        ... )
   338	    """
   339	    from nirs4all.synthesis import SyntheticDatasetBuilder
   340	
   341	    builder = SyntheticDatasetBuilder(
   342	        n_samples=n_samples,
   343	        random_state=random_state,
   344	        name=name,
   345	    )
   346	
   347	    builder.with_features(complexity=complexity)
   348	    builder.with_classification(
   349	        n_classes=n_classes,
   350	        separation=class_separation,
   351	        class_weights=class_weights,
   352	    )
   353	    builder.with_partitions(train_ratio=train_ratio)
   354	    builder.with_output(as_dataset=as_dataset)
   355	
   356	    return builder.build()
   357	
   358	def builder(
   359	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   360	    random_state: int | None = None,
   361	    name: str = "synthetic_nirs",
   362	) -> SyntheticDatasetBuilder:
   363	    """
   364	    Create a SyntheticDatasetBuilder for fine-grained control.
   365	
   366	    Use this when you need full control over all generation parameters
   367	    via the fluent builder interface.
   368	
   369	    Args:
   370	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   371	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   372	        name: Dataset name.
   373	
   374	    Returns:
   375	        SyntheticDatasetBuilder instance for method chaining.
   376	
   377	    Example:
   378	        >>> import nirs4all
   379	        >>>
   380	        >>> dataset = (
   381	        ...     nirs4all.generate.builder(n_samples=1000, random_state=42)
   382	        ...     .with_features(
   383	        ...         wavelength_range=(1000, 2500),
   384	        ...         complexity="realistic",
   385	        ...         components=["water", "protein", "lipid"]
   386	        ...     )
   387	        ...     .with_targets(
   388	        ...         distribution="lognormal",
   389	        ...         range=(5, 50),
   390	        ...         component="protein"
   391	        ...     )
   392	        ...     .with_metadata(n_groups=3)
   393	        ...     .with_partitions(train_ratio=0.8)
   394	        ...     .with_batch_effects(n_batches=3)
   395	        ...     .build()
   396	        ... )
   397	    """
   398	    from nirs4all.synthesis import SyntheticDatasetBuilder
   399	
   400	    return SyntheticDatasetBuilder(
   401	        n_samples=n_samples,
   402	        random_state=random_state,
   403	        name=name,
   404	    )
   405	
   406	def multi_source(
   407	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   408	    sources: list[dict[str, Any]] | None = None,
   409	    *,
   410	    random_state: int | None = None,
   411	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   412	    train_ratio: float = 0.8,
   413	    as_dataset: bool = True,
   414	    name: str = "multi_source_synthetic",
   415	) -> Any:
   416	    """
   417	    Generate a synthetic multi-source NIRS dataset.
   418	
   419	    Multi-source datasets combine different types of data, such as
   420	    multiple NIR spectral ranges or NIR spectra with auxiliary measurements.
   421	
   422	    Args:
   423	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   424	        sources: List of source configurations. Each source is a dict with:
   425	            - name: Unique source identifier (required).
   426	            - type: Source type - "nir", "vis", "aux", "markers" (default: "nir").
   427	            - wavelength_range: (start, end) for NIR sources.
   428	            - n_features: Number of features for auxiliary sources.
   429	            - complexity: Complexity level for NIR sources.
   430	            - components: Component names for NIR sources.
   431	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   432	        target_range: Optional (min, max) for scaling targets.
   433	        train_ratio: Proportion of samples for training partition.
   434	        as_dataset: If True, returns SpectroDataset. If False, returns (X, y).
   435	        name: Dataset name.
   436	
   437	    Returns:
   438	        If as_dataset=True: SpectroDataset with multiple sources.
   439	        If as_dataset=False: Tuple of (X, y) where X is concatenated features.
   440	
   441	    Example:
   442	        >>> import nirs4all
   443	        >>>
   444	        >>> # NIR + markers
   445	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.multi_source(
   446	        ...     n_samples=500,
   447	        ...     sources=[
   448	        ...         {"name": "NIR", "type": "nir", "wavelength_range": (1000, 2500)},
   449	        ...         {"name": "markers", "type": "aux", "n_features": 15}
   450	        ...     ],
   451	        ...     random_state=42
   452	        ... )
   453	        >>>
   454	        >>> # Multiple NIR ranges
   455	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.multi_source(
   456	        ...     n_samples=500,
   457	        ...     sources=[
   458	        ...         {"name": "VIS-NIR", "type": "nir", "wavelength_range": (400, 1100)},
   459	        ...         {"name": "SWIR", "type": "nir", "wavelength_range": (1100, 2500)}
   460	        ...     ]
   461	        ... )
   462	    """
   463	    from nirs4all.synthesis import generate_multi_source as _generate_multi_source
   464	
   465	    if sources is None:
   466	        # Default: NIR + markers
   467	        sources = [
   468	            {"name": "NIR", "type": "nir", "wavelength_range": (1000, 2500)},
   469	            {"name": "markers", "type": "aux", "n_features": 10}
   470	        ]
   471	
   472	    return _generate_multi_source(
   473	        n_samples=n_samples,
   474	        sources=sources,
   475	        random_state=random_state,
   476	        target_range=target_range,
   477	        as_dataset=as_dataset,
   478	        train_ratio=train_ratio,
   479	        name=name,
   480	    )
   481	
   482	def to_folder(
   483	    path: str | Path,
   484	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   485	    *,
   486	    random_state: int | None = None,
   487	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "simple",
   488	    train_ratio: float = 0.8,
   489	    format: Literal["standard", "single", "fragmented"] = "standard",
   490	    wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   491	    components: list[str] | None = None,
   492	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   493	) -> Path:
   494	    """
   495	    Generate synthetic data and export to a folder.
   496	
   497	    Creates a folder with CSV files compatible with nirs4all's
   498	    DatasetConfigs loader.
   499	
   500	    Args:
   501	        path: Output folder path.
   502	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   503	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   504	        complexity: Complexity level.
   505	        train_ratio: Train/test split ratio.
   506	        format: Export format ('standard', 'single', 'fragmented').
   507	        wavelength_range: Optional (start, end) wavelengths.
   508	        components: Optional list of component names.
   509	        target_range: Optional (min, max) for target scaling.
   510	
   511	    Returns:
   512	        Path to created folder.
   513	
   514	    Example:
   515	        >>> import nirs4all
   516	        >>> path = nirs4all.generate.to_folder(
   517	        ...     "data/synthetic",
   518	        ...     n_samples=1000,
   519	        ...     train_ratio=0.8,
   520	        ...     random_state=42
   521	        ... )
   522	    """
   523	    from nirs4all.synthesis import SyntheticDatasetBuilder
   524	
   525	    builder = SyntheticDatasetBuilder(
   526	        n_samples=n_samples,
   527	        random_state=random_state,
   528	    )
   529	
   530	    # Configure features
   531	    feature_kwargs: dict[str, Any] = {"complexity": complexity}
   532	    if wavelength_range is not None:
   533	        feature_kwargs["wavelength_range"] = wavelength_range
   534	    if components is not None:
   535	        feature_kwargs["components"] = components
   536	    builder.with_features(**feature_kwargs)
   537	
   538	    # Configure targets
   539	    if target_range is not None:
   540	        builder.with_targets(range=target_range)
   541	
   542	    # Configure partitions
   543	    builder.with_partitions(train_ratio=train_ratio)
   544	
   545	    return builder.export(path, format=format)
   546	
   547	def to_csv(
   548	    path: str | Path,
   549	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   550	    *,
   551	    random_state: int | None = None,
   552	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "simple",
   553	    wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   554	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   555	) -> Path:
   556	    """
   557	    Generate synthetic data and export to a single CSV file.
   558	
   559	    Args:
   560	        path: Output file path.
   561	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   562	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   563	        complexity: Complexity level.
   564	        wavelength_range: Optional (start, end) wavelengths.
   565	        target_range: Optional (min, max) for target scaling.
   566	
   567	    Returns:
   568	        Path to created file.
   569	
   570	    Example:
   571	        >>> import nirs4all
   572	        >>> path = nirs4all.generate.to_csv("data.csv", n_samples=500)
   573	    """
   574	    from nirs4all.synthesis import SyntheticDatasetBuilder
   575	
   576	    builder = SyntheticDatasetBuilder(
   577	        n_samples=n_samples,
   578	        random_state=random_state,
   579	    )
   580	
   581	    # Configure features
   582	    feature_kwargs: dict[str, Any] = {"complexity": complexity}
   583	    if wavelength_range is not None:
   584	        feature_kwargs["wavelength_range"] = wavelength_range
   585	    builder.with_features(**feature_kwargs)
   586	
   587	    # Configure targets
   588	    if target_range is not None:
   589	        builder.with_targets(range=target_range)
   590	
   591	    return builder.export_to_csv(path)
   592	
   593	def product(
   594	    template: str,
   595	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   596	    *,
   597	    target: str | None = None,
   598	    random_state: int | None = None,
   599	    wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   600	    wavelengths: np.ndarray | None = None,
   601	    instrument_wavelength_grid: str | None = None,
   602	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "realistic",
   603	    train_ratio: float = 0.8,
   604	    target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   605	) -> SpectroDataset:
   606	    """
   607	    Generate synthetic NIRS dataset from a product template.
   608	
   609	    Product templates define realistic compositions with controlled
   610	    variability for specific product types (dairy, grain, meat, pharma).
   611	    This is ideal for generating training data for neural networks.
   612	
   613	    Args:
   614	        template: Product template name (e.g., "milk_variable_fat",
   615	            "wheat_variable_protein", "tablet_variable_api").
   616	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   617	        target: Component to use as regression target.
   618	            If None, uses template's default target.
   619	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   620	        wavelength_range: Tuple of (start, end) wavelengths in nm.
   621	        wavelengths: Custom wavelength array.
   622	        instrument_wavelength_grid: Predefined instrument grid name
   623	            (e.g., "foss_xds", "micronir_onsite").
   624	        complexity: Spectral complexity level.
   625	        train_ratio: Proportion of samples for training partition.
   626	        target_range: Optional (min, max) to scale target values.
   627	
   628	    Returns:
   629	        SpectroDataset with train/test partitions.
   630	
   631	    Example:
   632	        >>> import nirs4all
   633	        >>>
   634	        >>> # Generate dairy samples for fat prediction
   635	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.product(
   636	        ...     "milk_variable_fat",
   637	        ...     n_samples=1000,
   638	        ...     target="lipid",
   639	        ...     random_state=42
   640	        ... )
   641	        >>>
   642	        >>> # Generate grain samples matching specific instrument
   643	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.product(
   644	        ...     "wheat_variable_protein",
   645	        ...     n_samples=5000,
   646	        ...     instrument_wavelength_grid="foss_xds"
   647	        ... )
   648	        >>>
   649	        >>> # List available templates
   650	        >>> from nirs4all.synthesis import list_product_templates
   651	        >>> print(list_product_templates(category="dairy"))
   652	
   653	    See Also:
   654	        generate.category: Generate from multiple product templates.
   655	        list_product_templates: List available templates.
   656	    """
   657	    from nirs4all.synthesis import ProductGenerator
   658	
   659	    # Build wavelength kwargs
   660	    wl_kwargs: dict[str, Any] = {"complexity": complexity}
   661	    if wavelength_range is not None:
   662	        wl_kwargs["wavelength_start"] = wavelength_range[0]
   663	        wl_kwargs["wavelength_end"] = wavelength_range[1]
   664	    if wavelengths is not None:
   665	        wl_kwargs["wavelengths"] = wavelengths
   666	    if instrument_wavelength_grid is not None:
   667	        wl_kwargs["instrument_wavelength_grid"] = instrument_wavelength_grid
   668	
   669	    generator = ProductGenerator(template, random_state=random_state, **wl_kwargs)
   670	
   671	    if target_range is not None:
   672	        return generator.generate_dataset_for_target(
   673	            target=target or generator.template.default_target,
   674	            n_samples=n_samples,
   675	            target_range=target_range,
   676	            train_ratio=train_ratio,
   677	        )
   678	    else:
   679	        result = generator.generate(
   680	            n_samples=n_samples,
   681	            target=target,
   682	            train_ratio=train_ratio,
   683	        )
   684	        return result[0] if isinstance(result, tuple) else result
   685	
   686	def category(
   687	    templates: list[str],
   688	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   689	    *,
   690	    target: str | None = None,
   691	    random_state: int | None = None,
   692	    samples_per_template: list[int] | None = None,
   693	    wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   694	    instrument_wavelength_grid: str | None = None,
   695	    complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "realistic",
   696	    train_ratio: float = 0.8,
   697	    shuffle: bool = True,
   698	) -> SpectroDataset:
   699	    """
   700	    Generate synthetic NIRS dataset from multiple product templates.
   701	
   702	    This creates training datasets that span multiple product types,
   703	    useful for building robust models that generalize across categories.
   704	
   705	    Args:
   706	        templates: List of product template names.
   707	        n_samples: Total number of samples to generate.
   708	        target: Component to use as regression target.
   709	            Must exist in all templates.
   710	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   711	        samples_per_template: Number of samples per template.
   712	            If None, divides equally.
   713	        wavelength_range: Tuple of (start, end) wavelengths in nm.
   714	        instrument_wavelength_grid: Predefined instrument grid name.
   715	        complexity: Spectral complexity level.
   716	        train_ratio: Proportion of samples for training partition.
   717	        shuffle: Whether to shuffle samples across templates.
   718	
   719	    Returns:
   720	        SpectroDataset combining samples from all templates.
   721	
   722	    Example:
   723	        >>> import nirs4all
   724	        >>>
   725	        >>> # Combine dairy products for fat prediction
   726	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.category(
   727	        ...     ["milk_variable_fat", "cheese_variable_moisture", "yogurt_variable_fat"],
   728	        ...     n_samples=3000,
   729	        ...     target="lipid",
   730	        ...     random_state=42
   731	        ... )
   732	        >>>
   733	        >>> # Universal protein predictor
   734	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.category(
   735	        ...     ["wheat_variable_protein", "soybean", "meat_variable_protein"],
   736	        ...     n_samples=10000,
   737	        ...     target="protein"
   738	        ... )
   739	
   740	    See Also:
   741	        generate.product: Generate from a single product template.
   742	    """
   743	    from nirs4all.synthesis import CategoryGenerator
   744	
   745	    # Build wavelength kwargs
   746	    wl_kwargs: dict[str, Any] = {"complexity": complexity}
   747	    if wavelength_range is not None:
   748	        wl_kwargs["wavelength_start"] = wavelength_range[0]
   749	        wl_kwargs["wavelength_end"] = wavelength_range[1]
   750	    if instrument_wavelength_grid is not None:
   751	        wl_kwargs["instrument_wavelength_grid"] = instrument_wavelength_grid
   752	
   753	    templates_arg: list[str | Any] = list(templates)
   754	    generator = CategoryGenerator(templates_arg, random_state=random_state, **wl_kwargs)
   755	
   756	    return generator.generate(
   757	        n_samples=n_samples,
   758	        target=target,
   759	        samples_per_template=samples_per_template,
   760	        train_ratio=train_ratio,
   761	        shuffle=shuffle,
   762	    )
   763	
   764	@overload
   765	def from_template(
   766	    template: str | np.ndarray | SpectroDataset,
   767	    n_samples: int = ...,
   768	    *,
   769	    random_state: int | None = ...,
   770	    wavelengths: np.ndarray | None = ...,
   771	    as_dataset: Literal[True] = ...,
   772	) -> SpectroDataset: ...
   773	
   774	@overload
   775	def from_template(
   776	    template: str | np.ndarray | SpectroDataset,
   777	    n_samples: int = ...,
   778	    *,
   779	    random_state: int | None = ...,
   780	    wavelengths: np.ndarray | None = ...,
   781	    as_dataset: Literal[False],
   782	) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]: ...
   783	
   784	def from_template(
   785	    template: str | np.ndarray | SpectroDataset,
   786	    n_samples: int = 1000,
   787	    *,
   788	    random_state: int | None = None,
   789	    wavelengths: np.ndarray | None = None,
   790	    as_dataset: bool = True,
   791	) -> SpectroDataset | tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
   792	    """
   793	    Generate synthetic data mimicking a real dataset template.
   794	
   795	    Analyzes the template data and generates synthetic spectra
   796	    with similar statistical and spectral properties.
   797	
   798	    Args:
   799	        template: Real data to mimic. Can be:
   800	            - Path to dataset folder (str).
   801	            - Numpy array (n_samples, n_wavelengths).
   802	            - SpectroDataset object.
   803	        n_samples: Number of samples to generate.
   804	        random_state: Random seed for reproducibility.
   805	        wavelengths: Wavelength grid (required if template is array).
   806	        as_dataset: If True, returns SpectroDataset. If False, returns (X, y).
   807	
   808	    Returns:
   809	        Synthetic dataset or arrays with properties similar to template.
   810	
   811	    Example:
   812	        >>> import nirs4all
   813	        >>>
   814	        >>> # From a dataset path
   815	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.from_template(
   816	        ...     "sample_data/regression",
   817	        ...     n_samples=1000
   818	        ... )
   819	        >>>
   820	        >>> # From numpy array
   821	        >>> dataset = nirs4all.generate.from_template(
   822	        ...     X_real,
   823	        ...     n_samples=500,
   824	        ...     wavelengths=wavelengths
   825	        ... )
   826	    """
   827	    from nirs4all.synthesis import RealDataFitter, SyntheticDatasetBuilder
   828	
   829	    builder = SyntheticDatasetBuilder(
   830	        n_samples=n_samples,
   831	        random_state=random_state,
   832	    )
   833	
   834	    # Handle string path
   835	    if isinstance(template, str):
   836	        from nirs4all.data import DatasetConfigs
   837	
   838	        dataset_config = DatasetConfigs(template)
   839	        datasets = dataset_config.get_datasets()
   840	        if not datasets:
   841	            raise ValueError(f"No datasets found at {template}")
   842	
   843	        template_ds = datasets[0]
   844	        template_array = np.asarray(template_ds.x({}, layout="2d"))
   845	        with contextlib.suppress(AttributeError, TypeError):
   846	            wavelengths = getattr(template_ds, 'wavelengths', None)
   847	        builder.fit_to(template_array, wavelengths=wavelengths)
   848	    else:
   849	        builder.fit_to(template, wavelengths=wavelengths)
   850	
   851	    builder.with_output(as_dataset=as_dataset)
   852	    return builder.build()
   853	
   854	class _GenerateNamespace:
   855	    """
   856	    Namespace class that makes generate both callable and a namespace.
   857	
   858	    This allows both:
   859	        nirs4all.generate(n_samples=1000)
   860	        nirs4all.generate.regression(n_samples=500)
   861	    """
   862	
   863	    if TYPE_CHECKING:
   864	        @overload
   865	        def __call__(
   866	            self,
   867	            n_samples: int = ...,
   868	            *,
   869	            random_state: int | None = ...,
   870	            complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
   871	            wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
   872	            components: list[str] | None = ...,
   873	            target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
   874	            train_ratio: float = ...,
   875	            as_dataset: Literal[True] = ...,
   876	            name: str = ...,
   877	            **kwargs: Any,
   878	        ) -> SpectroDataset: ...
   879	
   880	        @overload
   881	        def __call__(
   882	            self,
   883	            n_samples: int = ...,
   884	            *,
   885	            random_state: int | None = ...,
   886	            complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = ...,
   887	            wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
   888	            components: list[str] | None = ...,
   889	            target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = ...,
   890	            train_ratio: float = ...,
   891	            as_dataset: Literal[False],
   892	            name: str = ...,
   893	            **kwargs: Any,
   894	        ) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]: ...
   895	
   896	        def __call__(
   897	            self,
   898	            n_samples: int = 1000,
   899	            *,
   900	            random_state: int | None = None,
   901	            complexity: Literal["simple", "realistic", "complex"] = "simple",
   902	            wavelength_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   903	            components: list[str] | None = None,
   904	            target_range: tuple[float, float] | None = None,
   905	            train_ratio: float = 0.8,
   906	            as_dataset: bool = True,
   907	            name: str = "synthetic_nirs",
   908	            **kwargs: Any,
   909	        ) -> SpectroDataset | tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]: ...
   910	    else:
   911	        # Make the main generate function available as __call__
   912	        __call__ = staticmethod(generate)
   913	
   914	    # Convenience functions as class attributes
   915	    regression = staticmethod(regression)
   916	    classification = staticmethod(classification)
   917	    builder = staticmethod(builder)
   918	    multi_source = staticmethod(multi_source)
   919	
   920	    # Export functions (Phase 4)
   921	    to_folder = staticmethod(to_folder)
   922	    to_csv = staticmethod(to_csv)
   923	    from_template = staticmethod(from_template)
   924	
   925	    # Product-level generation (Phase 7)
   926	    product = staticmethod(product)
   927	    category = staticmethod(category)
   928	
   929	    def __repr__(self) -> str:
   930	        """Return string representation."""
   931	        return (
   932	            "<nirs4all.generate namespace>\n"
   933	            "  generate(n_samples, ...) - Generate synthetic NIRS dataset\n"
   934	            "  generate.regression(...) - Generate regression dataset\n"
   935	            "  generate.classification(...) - Generate classification dataset\n"
   936	            "  generate.multi_source(...) - Generate multi-source dataset\n"
   937	            "  generate.product(...) - Generate from product template (Phase 7)\n"
   938	            "  generate.category(...) - Generate from multiple templates (Phase 7)\n"
   939	            "  generate.builder(...) - Get fluent builder for full control\n"
   940	            "  generate.to_folder(...) - Generate and export to folder\n"
   941	            "  generate.to_csv(...) - Generate and export to CSV file\n"
   942	            "  generate.from_template(...) - Generate mimicking real data"
   943	        )
   944	
   945	# Create the singleton namespace instance
   946	# This replaces the module when imported
   947	generate_namespace = _GenerateNamespace()
   948	
   949	# For direct function access
   950	__all__ = [
   951	    "generate",
   952	    "regression",
   953	    "classification",
   954	    "builder",
   955	    "multi_source",
   956	    "to_folder",
   957	    "to_csv",
   958	    "from_template",
   959	    # Phase 7: Product-level generation
   960	    "product",
   961	    "category",
   962	    "generate_namespace",
   963	]

     1	"""
     2	NIRS4All API Module - High-level functional interface.
     3	
     4	This module provides the primary public API for nirs4all, offering
     5	simple function-based entry points that wrap the underlying PipelineRunner.
     6	
     7	Public API:
     8	    run(pipeline, dataset, **kwargs) -> RunResult
     9	        Execute a training pipeline on a dataset.
    10	
    11	    predict(model, data, **kwargs) -> PredictResult
    12	        Make predictions with a trained model.
    13	
    14	    explain(model, data, **kwargs) -> ExplainResult
    15	        Generate SHAP explanations for model predictions.
    16	
    17	    retrain(source, data, **kwargs) -> RunResult
    18	        Retrain a pipeline on new data.
    19	
    20	    session(**kwargs) -> Session
    21	        Create an execution session for resource reuse.
    22	
    23	    generate(n_samples, **kwargs) -> SpectroDataset | (X, y)
    24	        Generate synthetic NIRS data for testing and research.
    25	
    26	Example:
    27	    >>> import nirs4all
    28	    >>> from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
    29	    >>> from sklearn.cross_decomposition import PLSRegression
    30	    >>>
    31	    >>> result = nirs4all.run(
    32	    ...     pipeline=[MinMaxScaler(), PLSRegression(10)],
    33	    ...     dataset="sample_data/regression",
    34	    ...     verbose=1
    35	    ... )
    36	    >>> print(f"Best RMSE: {result.best_rmse:.4f}")
    37	
    38	For more examples, see the examples/Q40_new_api.py file.
    39	"""
    40	
    41	# Result classes (Phase 1)
    42	from .explain import explain
    43	
    44	# Synthetic data generation
    45	from .generate import generate_namespace as generate
    46	from .predict import predict
    47	from .result import ExplainResult, LazyModelRefitResult, ModelRefitResult, PredictResult, RunResult
    48	from .retrain import retrain
    49	
    50	# Module-level functions (Phase 2)
    51	from .run import run
    52	
    53	# Session (Phase 3 - full implementation)
    54	from .session import Session, load_session, session
    55	
    56	__all__ = [
    57	    # Module-level API functions
    58	    "run",
    59	    "predict",
    60	    "explain",
    61	    "retrain",
    62	    # Session
    63	    "Session",
    64	    "session",

    75	# Lazy loading for TensorFlow models
    76	_tensorflow_exports = None
    77	
    78	def _get_tensorflow_exports():
    79	    """Lazily load TensorFlow model exports."""
    80	    global _tensorflow_exports
    81	    if _tensorflow_exports is None:
    82	        from nirs4all.utils.backend import is_available
    83	        if is_available('tensorflow'):
    84	            from .tensorflow import generic, nicon
    85	            _tensorflow_exports = {}
    86	            # Collect all exported names from tensorflow modules
    87	            for mod in [nicon, generic]:
    88	                for name in getattr(mod, '__all__', []):
    89	                    _tensorflow_exports[name] = getattr(mod, name)
    90	        else:
    91	            _tensorflow_exports = {}
    92	    return _tensorflow_exports
    93	
    94	def __getattr__(name):
    95	    """Lazy attribute access for TensorFlow models."""
    96	    tf_exports = _get_tensorflow_exports()
    97	    if name in tf_exports:
    98	        return tf_exports[name]
    99	    raise AttributeError(f"module {__name__!r} has no attribute {name!r}")
   100

     1	from collections.abc import Sequence
     2	from typing import Any, Optional
     3	
     4	import flax.linen as nn
     5	import jax.numpy as jnp
     6	
     7	
     8	class JaxMLPRegressor(nn.Module):
     9	    """Simple MLP Regressor using Flax."""
    10	    features: Sequence[int]
    11	    input_shape: Any | None = None  # Ignored, but kept for compatibility with factory
    12	
    13	    @nn.compact
    14	    def __call__(self, x, train: bool = False):
    15	        # Flatten input if needed (batch, features...) -> (batch, flat_features)
    16	        if x.ndim > 2:
    17	            x = x.reshape((x.shape[0], -1))
    18	
    19	        for feat in self.features:
    20	            x = nn.Dense(feat)(x)
    21	            x = nn.relu(x)
    22	        # Output layer for regression (1 output)
    23	        x = nn.Dense(1)(x)
    24	        return x
    25	
    26	class JaxMLPClassifier(nn.Module):
    27	    """Simple MLP Classifier using Flax."""
    28	    features: Sequence[int]
    29	    num_classes: int
    30	    input_shape: Any | None = None # Ignored
    31	
    32	    @nn.compact
    33	    def __call__(self, x, train: bool = False):
    34	        # Flatten input if needed
    35	        if x.ndim > 2:
    36	            x = x.reshape((x.shape[0], -1))
    37	
    38	        for feat in self.features:
    39	            x = nn.Dense(feat)(x)
    40	            x = nn.relu(x)
    41	        # Output layer for classification (num_classes outputs)
    42	        x = nn.Dense(self.num_classes)(x)
    43	        return x

     1	"""
     2	U01 - Hello World: Your First nirs4all Pipeline
     3	================================================
     4	
     5	The simplest possible nirs4all pipeline in about 20 lines of code.
     6	
     7	This tutorial covers:
     8	
     9	* Using ``nirs4all.run()`` to train a pipeline
    10	* The structure of a minimal pipeline
    11	* Reading results from the ``RunResult`` object
    12	
    13	Prerequisites
    14	-------------
    15	None - this is the starting point!
    16	
    17	Next Steps
    18	----------
    19	After this example, see :ref:`U02_basic_regression` for preprocessing and visualization.
    20	
    21	Duration: ~1 minute
    22	Difficulty: ★☆☆☆☆
    23	"""
    24	
    25	# Standard library imports
    26	import argparse
    27	
    28	# Third-party imports
    29	from sklearn.cross_decomposition import PLSRegression
    30	from sklearn.model_selection import ShuffleSplit
    31	from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
    32	
    33	# NIRS4All imports
    34	import nirs4all
    35	
    36	# Parse command-line arguments
    37	parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description='U01 Hello World Example')
    38	parser.add_argument('--plots', action='store_true', help='Save plots')
    39	parser.add_argument('--show', action='store_true', help='Display plots interactively')
    40	args = parser.parse_args()
    41	
    42	# =============================================================================
    43	# Section 1: Define a Minimal Pipeline
    44	# =============================================================================
    45	print("\n" + "=" * 60)
    46	print("U01 - Hello World: Your First nirs4all Pipeline")
    47	print("=" * 60)
    48	
    49	# A pipeline is a simple list of processing steps
    50	pipeline = [
    51	    MinMaxScaler(),                              # Feature scaling
    52	    {"y_processing": MinMaxScaler()},            # Target scaling
    53	    ShuffleSplit(n_splits=3, test_size=0.25),    # Cross-validation
    54	    {"model": PLSRegression(n_components=10)}    # Model
    55	]
    56	
    57	print("\n📋 Pipeline defined:")
    58	print("   1. MinMaxScaler() - scale features to [0,1]")
    59	print("   2. y_processing - scale targets")
    60	print("   3. ShuffleSplit - 3-fold cross-validation")
    61	print("   4. PLSRegression - PLS model with 10 components")
    62	
    63	# =============================================================================
    64	# Section 2: Train the Pipeline
    65	# =============================================================================
    66	print("\n" + "-" * 60)
    67	print("Training the pipeline...")
    68	print("-" * 60)
    69	
    70	# Run the pipeline with one simple call
    71	result = nirs4all.run(
    72	    pipeline=pipeline,
    73	    dataset="sample_data/regression",
    74	    name="HelloWorld",
    75	    verbose=1,
    76	    save_artifacts=True,
    77	    save_charts=args.plots or args.show,
    78	    plots_visible=args.show
    79	)
    80	
    81	# =============================================================================
    82	# Section 3: Access Results
    83	# =============================================================================
    84	print("\n" + "-" * 60)
    85	print("Results")
    86	print("-" * 60)
    87	
    88	# The result object provides convenient accessors
    89	print("\n📊 Pipeline Results:")
    90	print(f"   Number of predictions: {result.num_predictions}")
    91	print(f"   Best Score (MSE): {result.best_score:.4f}")
    92	print(f"   Best RMSE: {result.best_rmse:.4f}")
    93	print(f"   Best R²: {result.best_r2:.4f}")
    94	
    95	# Get the best model details
    96	best = result.best
    97	if best:
    98	    print("\n🏆 Best Model Details:")
    99	    print(f"   Model name: {best.get('model_name', 'unknown')}")
   100	    print(f"   Dataset: {best.get('dataset_name', 'unknown')}")
   101	    print(f"   Fold: {best.get('fold_id', 'unknown')}")
   102	
   103	# =============================================================================
   104	# Section 4: Get Top Models
   105	# =============================================================================
   106	print("\n" + "-" * 60)
   107	print("Top 3 Models")
   108	print("-" * 60)
   109	
   110	# Get top predictions with display_metrics to include RMSE and R²
   111	for i, pred in enumerate(result.top(n=3, display_metrics=['rmse', 'r2']), 1):
   112	    rmse = pred.get('rmse', 0)
   113	    r2 = pred.get('r2', 0)
   114	    print(f"   {i}. {pred.get('model_name', 'unknown')} - RMSE: {rmse:.4f}, R²: {r2:.4f}")

   123	What we learned:
   124	1. A pipeline is a list of processing steps
   125	2. Use nirs4all.run() to train - no boilerplate needed
   126	3. Results are accessed via result.best_score, result.top(n), etc.
   127	
   128	Key API:
   129	  result = nirs4all.run(pipeline, dataset, name, ...)
   130	  result.best_score   # Best model's primary score

   132	  result.best_r2      # Best model's R²

     1	#!/usr/bin/env bash
     2	set -uo pipefail
     3	
     4	# =============================================================================
     5	# nirs4all Examples Runner
     6	# =============================================================================
     7	# Usage: ./run.sh [OPTIONS]
     8	#
     9	# Options:
    10	#   -i INDEX     Run single example by index (1-based)
    11	#   -b BEGIN     Start from this index (1-based)
    12	#   -e END       End at this index (1-based)
    13	#   -n NAME      Run by name pattern (glob, e.g., "U01*.py")
    14	#   -c CATEGORY  Category: user, developer, reference, all (default: all)
    15	#   -l           Enable logging to log.txt
    16	#   -p           Generate plots
    17	#   -s           Show plots interactively
    18	#   -h           Show this help message
    19	#
    20	# Examples:
    21	#   ./run.sh                     # Run all examples
    22	#   ./run.sh -c user             # Run only User path examples
    23	#   ./run.sh -i 1                # Run first example
    24	#   ./run.sh -n "U01*.py"        # Run by name pattern
    25	#   ./run.sh -l -p               # Enable logging and plots
    26	# =============================================================================
    27	
    28	INDEX=0
    29	BEGIN=0
    30	END=0
    31	NAME=""
    32	CATEGORY="all"
    33	LOG=0
    34	PLOT=0
    35	SHOW=0
    36	
    37	show_help() {
    38	  head -30 "$0" | tail -25 | sed 's/^# //' | sed 's/^#//'
    39	  exit 0
    40	}
    41	
    42	while getopts "i:b:e:n:c:lpsh" opt; do
    43	  case "$opt" in
    44	    i) INDEX="$OPTARG" ;;
    45	    b) BEGIN="$OPTARG" ;;
    46	    e) END="$OPTARG" ;;
    47	    n) NAME="$OPTARG" ;;
    48	    c) CATEGORY="$OPTARG" ;;
    49	    l) LOG=1 ;;
    50	    p) PLOT=1 ;;
    51	    s) SHOW=1 ;;
    52	    h) show_help ;;
    53	    *) echo "Usage: $0 [-i index] [-b begin] [-e end] [-n name] [-c category] [-l] [-p] [-s] [-h]"; exit 1 ;;
    54	  esac
    55	done
    56	shift $((OPTIND -1))

   162	# Function to filter existing examples only
   163	filter_existing() {
   164	  local -n arr=$1
   165	  local filtered=()
   166	  for ex in "${arr[@]}"; do
   167	    if [ -f "$ex" ]; then
   168	      filtered+=("$ex")

   170	  done
   171	  arr=("${filtered[@]}")
   172	}

   190	      ;;
   191	    *)
   192	      echo "Error: Unknown category '$CATEGORY'. Valid: user, developer, reference, all" >&2
   193	      exit 1
   194	      ;;

   199	  for ex in "${examples[@]}"; do

   201	      existing+=("$ex")
   202	    fi
   203	  done
   204	
   205	  echo "${existing[@]}"
   206	}

     1	"""
     2	U06 - TabPFN for NIRS: a fixed recipe without HPO
     3	==================================================
     4	
     5	Use the TabPFN tabular foundation model on NIRS spectra with a fixed
     6	preprocessing chain (no per-dataset HPO).
     7	
     8	This tutorial covers:
     9	
    10	* What :class:`TabPFNNIRSRegressor` does (recipe + rationale)
    11	* When to use it vs PLS / AOM-PLS / CNN models
    12	* Quick fit/predict on the bundled sample dataset
    13	* How to tweak ``n_estimators``, ``max_features``, and other knobs
    14	
    15	The recipe at a glance
    16	----------------------
    17	``SavitzkyGolay(11, 2, 1)`` ▶ ``OSC()`` ▶ centering ▶
    18	``TabPFNRegressor(n_estimators=16)``
    19	
    20	It was selected by extracting the most-frequent winning preprocessing
    21	motif from the TabPFN paper logs (deriv-1 SG with OSC correction) and
    22	empirically validating ``n_estimators=16`` on a 57-dataset NIRS cohort.
    23	On that cohort, the median test-set RMSE lands at +2.5% versus the
    24	TabPFN paper's 72-chain per-dataset HPO baseline ``TabPFN_opt`` -- at a
    25	single TabPFN training per dataset.
    26	
    27	Prerequisites
    28	-------------
    29	- ``pip install tabpfn`` (optional dependency)
    30	- A working GPU is recommended for n_train > 200 (TabPFN runs on CPU but
    31	  much faster on CUDA / MPS).
    32	
    33	Next Steps
    34	----------
    35	For HPO across multiple chains (PLS variants, AOM, etc.), see
    36	:ref:`U02_hyperparameter_tuning`. For ensemble / stacking, see
    37	:ref:`U03_stacking_ensembles`.
    38	
    39	Duration: ~3 minutes
    40	Difficulty: ★★☆☆☆
    41	"""
    42	
    43	# Standard library
    44	import argparse
    45	
    46	# Third-party
    47	import numpy as np
    48	from sklearn.model_selection import ShuffleSplit
    49	
    50	# nirs4all
    51	import nirs4all
    52	from nirs4all.operators.models import TabPFNNIRSRegressor
    53	
    54	parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="U06 TabPFN NIRS recipe")
    55	parser.add_argument("--plots", action="store_true", help="Generate plots")
    56	parser.add_argument("--show", action="store_true", help="Display plots interactively")
    57	args = parser.parse_args()
    58	
    59	
    60	# =============================================================================
    61	# Section 1: Why TabPFNNIRSRegressor?
    62	# =============================================================================
    63	
    64	print("\n" + "=" * 60)
    65	print("U06 - TabPFN for NIRS")
    66	print("=" * 60)
    67	print("""
    68	TabPFN is a transformer-based tabular foundation model that achieves
    69	state-of-the-art on many small-to-medium tabular regression / classification
    70	tasks without per-dataset hyperparameter tuning.
    71	
    72	On NIRS spectra, the choice of preprocessing matters more than for tabular
    73	data. The TabPFN paper runs an HPO sweep over 72 preprocessing chains per
    74	dataset and keeps the best (``TabPFN_opt``); this is expensive.
    75	
    76	``TabPFNNIRSRegressor`` instead uses ONE fixed preprocessing recipe selected
    77	empirically. It matches ``TabPFN_opt`` within ~2.5% RMSE in median on a
    78	57-dataset NIRS cohort, at a fraction of the cost (no HPO, one TabPFN fit).
    79	""")
    80	
    81	
    82	# =============================================================================
    83	# Section 2: The recipe under the hood
    84	# =============================================================================
    85	
    86	print("-" * 60)
    87	print("Section 2: Fixed recipe (no HPO)")
    88	print("-" * 60)
    89	
    90	est = TabPFNNIRSRegressor()
    91	print("Default hyperparameters:")
    92	for k, v in est.get_params().items():
    93	    print(f"  {k:22s} = {v}")
    94	print("""
    95	Internally the estimator applies in sequence:
    96	  1. SavitzkyGolay(window_length=11, polyorder=2, deriv=1)
    97	  2. OSC(n_components=1)
    98	  3. linspace subsample to <= 2000 columns (TabPFN v3 hard limit)
    99	  4. center (with_std=False)
   100	  5. TabPFNRegressor(n_estimators=16, ignore_pretraining_limits=True)
   101	""")
   102	
   103	
   104	# =============================================================================
   105	# Section 3: Run on the bundled sample dataset via nirs4all.run()
   106	# =============================================================================
   107	
   108	print("-" * 60)
   109	print("Section 3: Pipeline integration")
   110	print("-" * 60)
   111	
   112	pipeline = [
   113	    ShuffleSplit(n_splits=2, test_size=0.2, random_state=42),
   114	    {"model": TabPFNNIRSRegressor(n_estimators=8)},  # n_est=8 for example speed
   115	]
   116	
   117	result = nirs4all.run(
   118	    pipeline=pipeline,
   119	    dataset="examples/sample_data/regression",
   120	    verbose=0,
   121	    random_state=42,
   122	    name="U06_TabPFN_NIRS",
   123	)
   124	print(f"  best RMSE = {result.best_rmse:.4f}")
   125	print(f"  best R^2  = {result.best_r2:.4f}")

   139	wavelengths = np.linspace(0.0, 1.0, p)
   140	baseline = np.exp(-((wavelengths - 0.5) ** 2) / 0.01)

     1	"""
     2	U02 - Basic Regression: NIRS Preprocessing and Model Comparison
     3	================================================================
     4	
     5	A complete regression pipeline with NIRS-specific preprocessing and visualization.
     6	
     7	This tutorial covers:
     8	
     9	* NIRS-specific preprocessing (SNV, Detrend, Derivatives, Gaussian)
    10	* Feature augmentation to explore preprocessing combinations
    11	* Using ``PredictionAnalyzer`` for result visualization
    12	* Comparing models with different n_components
    13	
    14	Prerequisites
    15	-------------
    16	Complete :ref:`U01_hello_world` first.
    17	
    18	Next Steps
    19	----------
    20	See :ref:`U03_basic_classification` for classification tasks.
    21	
    22	Duration: ~3 minutes
    23	Difficulty: ★★☆☆☆
    24	"""
    25	
    26	# Standard library imports
    27	import argparse
    28	
    29	import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
    30	
    31	# Third-party imports
    32	from sklearn.cross_decomposition import PLSRegression
    33	from sklearn.model_selection import ShuffleSplit
    34	from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
    35	
    36	# NIRS4All imports
    37	import nirs4all
    38	from nirs4all.operators.transforms import Detrend, FirstDerivative, Gaussian, Haar, MultiplicativeScatterCorrection, SavitzkyGolay, StandardNormalVariate
    39	from nirs4all.visualization.predictions import PredictionAnalyzer
    40	
    41	# Parse command-line arguments
    42	parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description='U02 Basic Regression Example')
    43	parser.add_argument('--plots', action='store_true', help='Save plots')
    44	parser.add_argument('--show', action='store_true', help='Display plots interactively')
    45	args = parser.parse_args()
    46	
    47	# =============================================================================
    48	# Section 1: Define Preprocessing Options
    49	# =============================================================================
    50	print("\n" + "=" * 60)
    51	print("U02 - Basic Regression Pipeline")
    52	print("=" * 60)
    53	
    54	print("\n📋 NIRS Preprocessing Options:")
    55	print("   • StandardNormalVariate (SNV) - scatter correction")
    56	print("   • MultiplicativeScatterCorrection (MSC) - scatter correction")
    57	print("   • Detrend - baseline correction")
    58	print("   • FirstDerivative - removes baseline, enhances peaks")
    59	print("   • SavitzkyGolay - smoothing with differentiation")
    60	print("   • Gaussian - smoothing filter")
    61	print("   • Haar - wavelet transform")
    62	
    63	# =============================================================================
    64	# Section 2: Build the Pipeline
    65	# =============================================================================
    66	print("\n" + "-" * 60)
    67	print("Building Pipeline")
    68	print("-" * 60)
    69	
    70	# Build the pipeline with feature augmentation
    71	pipeline = [
    72	    # Feature scaling
    73	    MinMaxScaler(),
    74	
    75	    # Target scaling
    76	    {"y_processing": MinMaxScaler()},
    77	
    78	    # Feature augmentation: generate preprocessing combinations
    79	    # This creates multiple variants with different preprocessing chains
    80	    {
    81	        "feature_augmentation": {
    82	            "_or_": [Detrend, FirstDerivative, Gaussian, SavitzkyGolay, Haar],
    83	            "pick": 2,      # Pick 2 at a time
    84	            "count": 3      # Generate 3 combinations
    85	        }
    86	    },
    87	
    88	    # Visualization (saved with --plots, shown interactively with --show)
    89	    "chart_2d",
    90	
    91	    # Cross-validation
    92	    ShuffleSplit(n_splits=3, test_size=0.25),
    93	]
    94	
    95	# Add PLS models with different numbers of components
    96	for n_components in [5, 10, 15]:
    97	    pipeline.append({
    98	        "name": f"PLS-{n_components}",
    99	        "model": PLSRegression(n_components=n_components)
   100	    })
   101	
   102	print("Pipeline includes:")
   103	print("   • MinMaxScaler for feature and target scaling")
   104	print("   • Feature augmentation with 3 preprocessing combinations")
   105	print("   • 3 PLS models (5, 10, 15 components)")
   106	
   107	# =============================================================================
   108	# Section 3: Train the Pipeline
   109	# =============================================================================
   110	print("\n" + "-" * 60)
   111	print("Training Pipeline")
   112	print("-" * 60)
   113	
   114	result = nirs4all.run(
   115	    pipeline=pipeline,
   116	    dataset="sample_data/regression",
   117	    name="BasicRegression",
   118	    verbose=1,
   119	    save_artifacts=True,
   120	    save_charts=args.plots or args.show,
   121	    plots_visible=args.show
   122	)
   123	
   124	print("\n📊 Training complete!")
   125	print(f"   Generated {result.num_predictions} predictions")

    94	
    95	def _freeze_group_value(value: Any) -> Any:
    96	    """Normalize a group label into a stable, hashable key."""
    97	    if isinstance(value, np.generic):
    98	        value = value.item()
    99	
   100	    if value is None:
   101	        return ("__missing__", "none")
   102	
   103	    if isinstance(value, (float, np.floating)) and np.isnan(value):
   104	        return ("__missing__", "nan")
   105	
   106	    if isinstance(value, np.ndarray):
   107	        value = value.tolist()
   108	
   109	    if isinstance(value, list):
   110	        return tuple(_freeze_group_value(item) for item in value)
   111	
   112	    if isinstance(value, tuple):
   113	        return tuple(_freeze_group_value(item) for item in value)
   114	
   115	    return value
   116	
   117	
   118	def _build_group_constraint(
   119	    dataset: SpectroDataset,
   120	    columns: list[str],
   121	    context: Any | None,
   122	    include_augmented: bool,
   123	) -> np.ndarray:
   124	    """Return one grouping constraint from one or more metadata columns."""
   125	    if len(columns) == 1:
   126	        return dataset.metadata_column(
   127	            columns[0],
   128	            context,
   129	            include_augmented=include_augmented,
   130	        )
   131	
   132	    arrays = [
   133	        dataset.metadata_column(col, context, include_augmented=include_augmented)
   134	        for col in columns
   135	    ]
   136	    tuple_groups = [tuple(row) for row in zip(*arrays, strict=False)]
   137	    groups = np.empty(len(tuple_groups), dtype=object)
   138	    groups[:] = tuple_groups
   139	    return groups
   140	
   141	
   142	def _compute_connected_group_components(
   143	    constraints: list[np.ndarray],
   144	) -> np.ndarray:
   145	    """Resolve multiple grouping constraints into connected component labels."""
   146	    if not constraints:
   147	        return np.array([], dtype=int)
   148	
   149	    n_samples = len(constraints[0])
   150	    if any(len(constraint) != n_samples for constraint in constraints):
   151	        raise ValueError("All grouping constraints must have the same length.")
   152	
   153	    parent = list(range(n_samples))
   154	
   155	    def find(index: int) -> int:
   156	        while parent[index] != index:
   157	            parent[index] = parent[parent[index]]
   158	            index = parent[index]
   159	        return index
   160	
   161	    def union(left: int, right: int) -> None:
   162	        root_left = find(left)
   163	        root_right = find(right)
   164	        if root_left != root_right:
   165	            parent[root_right] = root_left
   166	
   167	    for constraint in constraints:
   168	        first_seen_by_value: dict[Any, int] = {}
   169	        for sample_idx, raw_value in enumerate(constraint):
   170	            value = _freeze_group_value(raw_value)
   171	            first_idx = first_seen_by_value.get(value)
   172	            if first_idx is None:
   173	                first_seen_by_value[value] = sample_idx
   174	            else:
   175	                union(first_idx, sample_idx)
   176	
   177	    component_ids = np.empty(n_samples, dtype=int)
   178	    root_to_component: dict[int, int] = {}
   179	    next_component_id = 0
   180	
   181	    for sample_idx in range(n_samples):
   182	        root = find(sample_idx)
   183	        component_id = root_to_component.get(root)
   184	        if component_id is None:
   185	            component_id = next_component_id
   186	            root_to_component[root] = component_id
   187	            next_component_id += 1
   188	        component_ids[sample_idx] = component_id
   189	
   190	    return component_ids
   191	
   192	def compute_effective_groups(
   193	    dataset: SpectroDataset,
   194	    group_by: str | list[str] | None = None,
   195	    ignore_repetition: bool = False,
   196	    context: Any | None = None,
   197	    include_augmented: bool = False
   198	) -> np.ndarray | None:
   199	    """Compute final group labels for splitting.
   200	
   201	    Applies repetition and explicit ``group_by`` columns as split constraints.
   202	    When both are present, the effective groups are the connected components
   203	    induced by:
   204	    - same repetition value
   205	    - same explicit ``group_by`` value (or tuple of values for multi-column
   206	      ``group_by``)
   207	
   208	    This is stricter than a plain tuple of ``(repetition, group_by)`` because
   209	    it guarantees that raw ``group_by`` values cannot leak across folds when
   210	    the dataset repetition column is also enforced.
   211	
   212	    Parameters
   213	    ----------
   214	    dataset : SpectroDataset
   215	        The dataset containing metadata columns for grouping.
   216	    group_by : str or List[str], optional
   217	        Additional column(s) to group by. Combined with repetition
   218	        column if repetition is defined and not ignored.
   219	    ignore_repetition : bool, default=False
   220	        If True, ignore the dataset's repetition column and only use

     1	"""Controller router for selecting appropriate controllers."""
     2	from typing import Any
     3	
     4	from nirs4all.controllers.controller import OperatorController
     5	from nirs4all.controllers.registry import CONTROLLER_REGISTRY
     6	from nirs4all.pipeline.steps.parser import ParsedStep
     7	
     8	
     9	class ControllerRouter:
    10	    """Routes parsed steps to appropriate controllers.
    11	
    12	    Uses registry pattern with controller priorities.
    13	    Extensible - new controllers automatically discovered via registry.
    14	
    15	    Attributes:
    16	        registry: Controller registry (from nirs4all.controllers.registry)
    17	        verbose: If True, print debug information about controller matching
    18	    """
    19	
    20	    def __init__(self, verbose: bool = False):
    21	        """Initialize router with controller registry.
    22	
    23	        Args:
    24	            verbose: If True, print debug information about controller matching
    25	        """
    26	        self.registry = CONTROLLER_REGISTRY
    27	        self.verbose = verbose
    28	
    29	    def route(self, parsed_step: ParsedStep, step: Any = None) -> OperatorController:
    30	        """Select the appropriate controller for a parsed step.
    31	
    32	        Args:
    33	            parsed_step: Parsed step configuration
    34	            step: Original step (for backward compatibility with matches())
    35	
    36	        Returns:
    37	            Instantiated controller instance
    38	
    39	        Raises:
    40	            TypeError: If no matching controller found
    41	        """
    42	        # Use original step for matching if available
    43	        match_step = step if step is not None else parsed_step.original_step
    44	        operator = parsed_step.operator
    45	        keyword = parsed_step.keyword
    46	
    47	        if self.verbose:
    48	            print(f"\n[Router] Matching step: {match_step}")
    49	            print(f"[Router]   Operator: {operator}")
    50	            print(f"[Router]   Keyword: {keyword}")
    51	
    52	        # Find all matching controllers
    53	        matches = []
    54	        for cls in self.registry:
    55	            matched = cls.matches(match_step, operator, keyword)
    56	            if self.verbose:
    57	                status = "✓" if matched else "✗"
    58	                print(f"[Router]   {status} {cls.__name__} (priority={cls.priority})")
    59	            if matched:
    60	                matches.append(cls)
    61	
    62	        if not matches:
    63	            raise TypeError(
    64	                f"No matching controller found for step: {match_step}. "
    65	                f"Operator: {operator}, Keyword: {keyword}. "
    66	                f"Available controllers: {[cls.__name__ for cls in self.registry]}"
    67	            )
    68	
    69	        # Sort by priority (lower number = higher priority)
    70	        matches.sort(key=lambda c: c.priority)
    71	
    72	        if self.verbose:
    73	            print(f"[Router] Selected: {matches[0].__name__} (priority={matches[0].priority})")
    74	
    75	        # Return instantiated controller with highest priority
    76	        return matches[0]()
    77

   475	class CrossValidatorController(OperatorController):
   476	    """Controller for **any** sklearn‑compatible splitter (native or custom)."""
   477	
   478	    priority = 10  # processed early but after mandatory pre‑processing steps
   479	
   480	    @classmethod
   481	    def matches(cls, step: Any, operator: Any, keyword: str) -> bool:  # noqa: D401
   482	        """Return *True* if *operator* behaves like a splitter.
   483	
   484	        **Criteria** – must expose a callable ``split`` whose first positional
   485	        argument is named *X*.  Optional presence of ``get_n_splits`` is a plus
   486	        but not mandatory, so user‑defined simple splitters are still accepted.
   487	
   488	        Also matches on the 'split' keyword for group-aware splitting syntax.
   489	        """
   490	        # Priority 1: Match on 'split' keyword (explicit workflow operator)
   491	        if keyword == "split":
   492	            return True
   493	
   494	        # Priority 2: Match dict with 'split' key
   495	        if isinstance(step, dict) and "split" in step:
   496	            return True
   497	
   498	        # Priority 3: Match objects with split() method (existing behavior)
   499	        if operator is None:
   500	            return False
   501	
   502	        split_fn = getattr(operator, "split", None)
   503	        if not callable(split_fn):
   504	            return False
   505	        try:
   506	            sig = inspect.signature(split_fn)
   507	        except (TypeError, ValueError):  # edge‑cases: C‑extensions or cythonised
   508	            return True  # accept – we can still attempt runtime call
   509	        params: list[inspect.Parameter] = [
   510	            p for p in sig.parameters.values()
   511	            if p.kind in (p.POSITIONAL_ONLY, p.POSITIONAL_OR_KEYWORD)
   512	        ]
   513	        return bool(params) and params[0].name == "X"
   514	
   515	    @classmethod
   516	    def use_multi_source(cls) -> bool:  # noqa: D401
   517	        """Cross‑validators themselves are single‑source operators."""
   518	        return False
   519	
   520	    @classmethod
   521	    def supports_prediction_mode(cls) -> bool:
   522	        """Cross-validators should not execute during prediction mode."""
   523	        return True
   524	
   525	    def execute(
   526	        self,
   527	        step_info: ParsedStep,
   528	        dataset: SpectroDataset,
   529	        context: ExecutionContext,
   530	        runtime_context: RuntimeContext,
   531	        source: int = -1,
   532	        mode: str = "train",
   533	        loaded_binaries: Any = None,
   534	        prediction_store: Any = None
   535	    ):
   536	        """Run ``operator.split`` and store the resulting folds on *dataset*.
   537	
   538	        * Smartly supplies ``y`` / ``groups`` only if required.
   539	        * Extracts groups from metadata if specified.
   540	        * Supports ``group_by`` parameter and dataset repetition for group-aware splitting.
   541	        * Maps local indices back to the global index space.
   542	        * Stores the list of folds into the dataset for subsequent steps.
   543	
   544	        Parameters
   545	        ----------
   546	        step_info : ParsedStep
   547	            Parsed step containing the operator and original step configuration.
   548	        dataset : SpectroDataset
   549	            The dataset to split.
   550	        context : ExecutionContext
   551	            Current execution context.
   552	        runtime_context : RuntimeContext
   553	            Runtime context with global settings.
   554	        source : int
   555	            Source index (-1 for combined sources).
   556	        mode : str
   557	            Execution mode ("train", "predict", or "explain").
   558	        loaded_binaries : Any
   559	            Pre-loaded binary data (not used).
   560	        prediction_store : Any

   182	
   183	for name, method in methods.items():
   184	    pipeline = [method, ShuffleSplit(n_splits=3), PLSRegression(n_components=10)]
   185	    result = nirs4all.run(pipeline=pipeline, dataset="sample_data/regression")
   186	    print(f"{name}: RMSE = {result.best_rmse:.4f}")
   187	```
   188	
   189	---
   190
